(۲) قوله : كأبي الحسن القدوري " كذا في النسخة التي بيدى، وكذا في نسخ القدوري، وهو غلط فاحش صدر من النساخ، والصحيح أبي الحسين، كما في
"الكشف" ، و "الجواهر" ، و "الفوائد" ، و "وفيات الأعيان" . فليحفظ . واعلم أنه جعل القدورى وصاحب "الهداية " من أصحاب الترجيح، وقاضيخان من المجتهدين، مع تقدم القدوري على شمس الأئمة زمانًا، وكونه أعلى منه كعبا ، وأطول باعا، فكيف من قاضيخان . وأما صاحب الهداية : فهو المشار إليه في عصره، والمعقود عليه الخناصر في دهره ، وقد أقر له أهل عصره بالفضل والتقدم كالإمام فخر الدین قاضيخان وزين الدين ،وغيرهما، و قالوا : إنه فاق على أقرانه حتى على شيوخه في الفقه، فكيف ينزل عن شأنه عين قاضيخان؟ بل هو أحق منه بالاجتهاد وأثبت في أسبابه وألزم لأبوابه. فالإنصاف أن يعد من المجتهدين في المذهب، وهذا إلى العقل السليم أقرب . (مظ) وأجاب عنه بعض المحققين : بأن هذا الإشكال إنما نشأ مما يزعمه بعض الناس أن هذه الطبقات أقسام متباينة لا تجتمع في شخص واحد، فمن كان من أهل الترجيح لا يكون من أهل التخريج ، ومن كان من أهل التخريج لا يكون مجتهداً في المسائل. لكن الظاهر أن هذه الأقسام للوظائف لا للأشخاص، والمراد أن وظائف الفقهاء تنقسم إلى هذه الأقسام السبعة، ولا يستلزم من ذلك أن لا يكون الرجل يتولى جميع
Layers of Jurists
For they are unable to perform ijtihad at all, but due to their comprehensive knowledge of principles (usul) and their mastery of sources, they are able to detail a general statement that has two aspects, and a ruling that is probable for two matters, transmitted from the founder of the madhhab or from one of his mujtahid companions, by their opinion and consideration of the principles, and by analogy with similar and parallel subsidiary matters. And what occurs in some places of al-Hidayah from his saying: "Thus in the takhrij of al-Karkhi."
(Y):: The author (may Allah have mercy on him) counted him among the muqallids who cannot perform ijtihad at all, and this is a downgrading of Abu Bakr al-Razi from his lofty station. For his standing in knowledge is great, his capacity in fiqh is extensive, his rank in usul is high, his foot is firm therein, his tread is strong, and his grip is powerful. Whoever follows his works and the statements transmitted from him knows that those whom he counted among the mujtahids, from Shams al-A'imma and after him, are all dependent on Abu Bakr al-Razi. The proof of that is the evidence he set up for his choices and the proofs by which he revealed aspects of his arguments. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said about him: "He is a great man known in knowledge, and we indeed follow him (taqlid) and take his statement." So how can Ibn Kamal Pasha make Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, the author of this statement, a mujtahid in issues, and Abu Bakr al-Razi a muqallid unable to perform ijtihad at all? This would imply that Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, while being a mujtahid, follows (yuqallid) Abu Bakr al-Razi, who is a muqallid. It is possible to say: Ibn al-Kamal was confused by the statement of our scholars that his function is only takhrij, and that the utmost of his reach is this, while the mujtahid imams have produced many takhrij works, and that did not harm them in their ijtihad. So Abu Bakr al-Razi is likewise: his takhrij does not place him in a rank lower than his rank. Thus the truth is that he should be counted among the mujtahids in the madhhab. And Allah knows best. (maz)
(1) His saying: "to detail a general statement having two aspects" — thus did the scholar Ibn Kamal Pasha define the people of takhrij. It may be added that the people of takhrij sometimes derive specific subsidiary rulings from the statements of their imam, as will come in the explanation of the fifth couplet and after.
(2) His saying: "and what occurs in some places of al-Hidayah" — the author of al-Hidayah said in the chapter of dower under the statement of al-Jami' al-Saghir: "Whoever marries a woman then they differ about the dower..." his text: "and he explained their statement regarding when they differ during the existence of marriage... then he said: this is the takhrij of al-Razi, and al-Karkhi said... etc." And similar to this is what the author (may Allah have mercy on him) mentioned in his gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar in the book of the hermaphrodite.
[PAGE_048]
Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti
48
Layers of Jurists
"And the takhrij of al-Razi is of this type."
The fifth layer: the people of takhrij among the muqallids, such as Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri (2) and the author of al-Hidayah, and their like. Their function is to prefer some narrations.
(2) Under the statement of the matn: "He has the lesser of the two shares, and they said: half of the two shares" — his text: "His saying: 'and they said: half of the two shares' meaning half of the total of the male and female portions. Then know that this is the statement of al-Sha'bi. And since he was among the teachers of Abu Hanifa and had an ambiguous statement in this chapter, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differed in its takhrij. So it is not a statement of theirs because what is in al-Sirajiyya is that the statement of Abu Hanifa is the statement of his companions, and it is the statement of the majority of the Companions, and on it is the fatwa. (6/730)
(1) His saying: "takhrij" — this is in the copy I have, but the correct here is "tarjih" instead, as transmitted from Ibn al-Kamal in various places and as mentioned by the author in his gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
6
(2) His saying: "like Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri" — this is in the copy in my hand, and likewise in copies of al-Quduri, but it is a flagrant error that occurred from the copyists. The correct is Abu al-Husayn, as in al-Kashf, al-Jawahir, al-Fawa'id, and Wafayat al-A'yan. So let it be remembered. And know that he made al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah among the people of tarjih, and Qadikhan among the mujtahids, despite al-Quduri being earlier than Shams al-A'imma in time, and being higher in rank and more extensive in capacity, so how much more than Qadikhan? As for the author of al-Hidayah: he is the one pointed to in his era, the one upon whom fingers are tied in his time, and his contemporaries acknowledged his virtue and precedence, such as al-Imam Fakhr al-Din Qadikhan and Zayn al-Din and others. They said: he surpassed his peers, even his teachers, in fiqh. So how can he be lowered from his status by Qadikhan? Rather, he is more deserving of ijtihad than him, more established in its means, and more committed to its doors. Thus fairness dictates that he be counted among the mujtahids in the madhhab, and this is closer to sound reason. (maz)
And some investigators responded: this objection arose only from some people's assumption that these layers are distinct categories that do not combine in a single person, so that whoever is among the people of tarjih is not among the people of takhrij, and whoever is among the people of takhrij is not a mujtahid in issues. But the apparent view is that these categories are for functions, not persons, and the meaning is that the functions of jurists are divided into these seven categories, and that does not necessitate that a person cannot undertake all of them.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a critical examination of Ibn Kamal Pasha's classification of jurists, specifically the fifth layer: ashab al-takhrij (people of legal derivation). The author defends Abu Bakr al-Razi (the famous Hanafi jurist) against being relegated to the rank of a mere muqallid. The text opens by describing the function of the fifth layer: they cannot perform independent ijtihad but can elaborate on concise statements and derive rulings by applying principles and analogy. Ibn Kamal Pasha counted Abu Bakr al-Razi among these muqallids. However, the commentator objects vigorously, arguing that al-Razi's extensive works, his ability to set up proofs for his choices, and the testimony of Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani—who said 'we do taqlid of him and take his words'—prove that al-Razi was a mujtahid within the madhhab. The commentator points out the inconsistency: if al-Halwani (a mujtahid) follows al-Razi, then al-Razi cannot be a mere muqallid. He suggests Ibn Kamal was misled by the idea that takhrij is the only function of these jurists, but takhrij does not preclude ijtihad. The passage also includes textual corrections: the correct name is Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri (not Abu al-Hasan), and in some contexts 'tarjih' (preference) should replace 'takhrij'. The commentator further critiques Ibn Kamal for ranking Qadikhan above al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah, arguing that the latter are more deserving of ijtihad. Finally, a responding investigator suggests that these layers are functions, not personal grades, so one person may combine multiple functions. This passage exemplifies rasm al-mufti methodology by discussing the hierarchy of jurists and the standards for issuing fatwa.

Key Terms
التخريج (al-takhrij): The process of deriving a specific legal ruling from a general or ambiguous statement of a mujtahid by applying usul and analogy
المقلد (al-muqallid): A jurist who follows the rulings of a higher authority without independent reasoning
المجتهد في المذهب (al-mujtahid fi al-madhhab): A jurist who is not an absolute mujtahid but can derive rulings within the Hanafi school by using its principles

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the commentator object to Ibn Kamal Pasha placing Abu Bakr al-Razi in the fifth layer (ashab al-takhrij)?
A) Because Abu Bakr al-Razi was an absolute mujtahid outside the Hanafi madhhab
B) Because Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani, who is considered a mujtahid, said he follows al-Razi, indicating al-Razi's higher rank
C) Because al-Razi wrote many books and therefore cannot be a muqallid
D) Because Ibn Kamal Pasha was not a Hanafi

Key Takeaway
The seven layers of Hanafi jurists are functions, not exclusive ranks; a jurist like Abu Bakr al-Razi may combine takhrij and ijtihad, and should be classified accordingly.

Fifth Class: Ashab al-Tarjih and Correcting Textual Errors
Defining the fifth class and correcting textual errors

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fifth class of Hanafi muqallids, state its correct designation (tarjih vs. takhrij), and apply the correction to a common scribal error.

Core Idea
The fifth class are ashab al-tarjih, not ashab al-takhrij — their function is preferring narrations, not extrapolating.

Ibn Kamal Pasha's classification of Hanafi jurists includes seven classes. This lesson focuses on the fifth class, which the author initially labels 'ashab al-takhrij' but immediately corrects to 'ashab al-tarjih'. You will see how such terminological precision matters in the Hanafi tradition and how textual errors can mislead. The passage also provides an example of their work in inheritance rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the fifth class designation
Read the opening statement: 'الخامسة طبقة أصحاب التخريج'. Note that this is the class of muqallids who perform takhrij.
The author later corrects this to 'الترجيح' in the footnote.
2
Examine the correction from takhrij to tarjih
The footnote explicitly states that the correct term is 'الترجيح' (tarjih), meaning preference, not 'التخريج' (takhrij), meaning extrapolation. Understand why this distinction matters in Hanafi iftaa.
Tarjih involves choosing among existing narrations; takhrij involves deriving new rulings from weak narrations by analogy.
3
Analyze the example of inheritance shares
The text gives an example: 'وله أقل النصيبين وقالا : نصف النصيبين'. This is a case where the ruling involves preferring one narration over another. The author clarifies that the statement attributed to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is actually derived from al-Sha'bi, not their own view.
This shows how ashab al-tarjih work: they examine multiple narrations and prefer the stronger one.
4
Correct the scribal error in al-Quduri's name
The footnote corrects 'أبي الحسن' to 'أبي الحسين' for al-Quduri. Note the sources (al-Kashf, al-Jawahir, etc.) that verify this correction.
This illustrates the importance of manuscript verification in Hanafi texts.

The fifth class: the class of those who perform takhrij (or tarjih) from among the muqallids, such as Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah, and their likes. Their function is to prefer some narrations over others. (2) Under the statement of the matn: 'And he has the lesser of the two shares, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: half of the two shares', its text: 'His saying: And they said: half of the two shares' meaning half of the total share of the male and female. Then know that this is the statement of al-Sha'bi, and since he was among the teachers of Abu Hanifa and had an ambiguous statement in this chapter, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differed in his takhrij, so it is not their statement; because what is in al-Sirajiyyah is that the statement of Abu Hanifa is the statement of his companions, and it is the statement of the majority of the Companions, and the fatwa is upon it. (6/730) (1) His saying: 'al-takhrij' — thus in the copy I have, but the correct here is instead 'al-tarjih', as transmitted from Ibn al-Kamal in various places and as the author mentioned in his gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar. 6 (2) His saying: 'like Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri' — thus in the copy I have, and similarly in copies of al-Quduri, but it is a gross error from the scribes; the correct is Abu al-Husayn, as in al-Kashf, al-Jawahir, al-Fawa'id, and Wafayat al-A'yan. So let it be memorized. And know that he made al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah among the people of tarjih, and Qadi Khan among the mujtahids, despite al-Quduri being ahead of Shams al-A'imma in time, and being higher in rank and longer in reach — so how (could he be below) Qadi Khan? As for the author of al-Hidayah, he is the one referred to in his time, the one upon whom fingers are tied in his era, and his contemporaries acknowledged his excellence and precedence, such as Imam Fakhr al-Din Qadi Khan and Zayn al-Din and others, and they said: He surpassed his peers, even his teachers in fiqh, so how can his status be lowered compared to Qadi Khan? Rather, he is more deserving of ijtihad, more established in its means, and more committed to its doors. So fairness requires that he be counted among the mujtahids in the madhhab, and this is closer to sound reason. (Mz) And some verifiers answered: That this problem arises only from what some people claim that these classes are mutually exclusive divisions that cannot be combined in one person; so whoever is from the people of tarjih cannot be from the people of takhrij, and whoever is from the people of takhrij cannot be a mujtahid in issues. But the apparent is that these divisions are of functions, not persons; the meaning is that the functions of the jurists are divided into these seven categories, and it does not necessitate that a man cannot undertake all of these functions or some of them at one time. And this is like scholars being attributed as a mufassir, muhaddith, faqih, and mutakallim, but it may happen that one man is truthful in all these titles; he is, by virtue of his occupation with fiqh, a faqih; with the Quran, a mufassir; with hadith, a muhaddith. Similarly, it is permissible for one man to be a mujtahid in issues and also qualified for takhrij and tarjih at the same time.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth class of jurists according to Ibn Kamal Pasha's classification. The author begins by identifying them as 'ashab al-takhrij' (people of extrapolation) from among the muqallids, but immediately notes in the footnote that the correct term is 'ashab al-tarjih' (people of preference) based on Ibn al-Kamal's corrections. The text then gives an example of how these jurists work: they prefer some narrations over others, as illustrated by a discussion about the distribution of shares in inheritance between a male and female. The author clarifies that the statement attributed to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is not actually theirs; it was derived from al-Sha'bi's ambiguous statement, and the correct ruling is Abu Hanifa's and the majority of Companions. The footnote then corrects a scribal error: 'Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri' should be 'Abu al-Husayn'. There follows a significant discussion about the relative ranks of scholars: the author of the footnote questions why al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah are classified as ashab al-tarjih while Qadi Khan is considered a mujtahid, when the former two are arguably more learned. The response concludes that the author of al-Hidayah should rightfully be counted among the mujtahidin, not merely a muqallid. A further note explains that the seven classes describe functions, not individuals; one scholar can fulfill multiple roles. This is analogous to a scholar being both a mufassir, muhaddith, faqih, and mutakallim. Thus, the classification is about what jurists do, not fixed labels.

Key Terms
التخريج (al-takhrij): Extrapolating rulings from established principles; here the text corrects it to 'الترجيح' (preferring one narration over another).
الترجيح (al-tarjih): Preferring some narrations or rulings over others based on strength or other considerations.
المقلدين (al-muqallidin): Those who follow a madhhab without being able to derive rulings independently.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Ashab al-Tarjih

D) Ashab al-Ijtihad

Key Takeaway
The fifth class of Hanafi fuqaha are ashab al-tarjih, who prefer among narrations; scribal errors must be identified and corrected.

Functions vs. Persons: The Multi-Role Jurist
Resolving the ranking of al-Hidayah's author and explaining the functional nature of classes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain that Ibn Kamal Pasha's seven classes describe functions, not fixed ranks, and evaluate the claim that the author of al-Hidayah is not a mujtahid.

Core Idea
The seven classes are functional roles, not exclusive labels — one scholar can be a mujtahid, muqallid, and ashab al-tarjih simultaneously.

In this lesson, we delve into a common misconception arising from the classification of Hanafi jurists: that the classes are mutually exclusive. The passage uses the example of al-Quduri, the author of al-Hidayah, and Qadi Khan to argue that the author of al-Hidayah should be considered a mujtahid, not merely a muqallid. The resolution is that the classes describe functions, not persons.

Guided Path
1
Examine the ranking debate
The passage notes that al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah are classified as ashab al-tarjih, while Qadi Khan is considered a mujtahid. This seems unjust given al-Quduri's seniority and the author of al-Hidayah's clear expertise.
The author strongly argues that al-Hidayah's author is actually a mujtahid.
2
Understand the argument for al-Hidayah's mujtahid status
The text states that the author of al-Hidayah was acknowledged by his contemporaries (including Qadi Khan) as surpassing his peers and even his teachers in fiqh. Therefore, fairness demands he be counted among mujtahids.
This challenges the notion that the seventh class (mujtahid) is superior to the fifth; they are different functions.
3
Learn the principle: functions not persons
The passage resolves the apparent inconsistency: the seven classes are divisions of functions, not persons. One scholar can perform multiple functions (tarjih, takhrij, ijtihad) simultaneously.
This is akin to one scholar being both a mufassir and faqih.
4
Apply the analogy of scholarly titles
Just as a scholar can be called a mufassir, muhaddith, faqih, and mutakallim based on different aspects of his work, a jurist can be mujtahid and also engage in tarjih/takhrij.
This clarifies that classifications are about what a jurist does, not a rigid hierarchy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخامسة طبقة أصحاب التخريج (1) من المقلدين كأبي الحسن القدورى (٢) وصاحب الهداية" ، وأمثالهما . وشأنهم تفضيل بعض الروايات (۲) تحت قول الماتن : "وله أقل النصيبين وقالا : نصف النصيبين ما نصه: "قوله: وقالا : نصف النصيبين " أى نصف مجموع حظ الذكر والأنثى، ثم اعلم أن هذا قول الشعبي، ولما كان من أشياخ أبي حنيفة وله فى هذا الباب قول مبهم، اختلف أبو يوسف ومحمد في تخريجه ، فليس هو قولا لهما ؛ لأن الذي في السراجية أن قول أبي حنيفة هو قول أصحابه، وهو قول عامة الصحابة، وعليه الفتوى . (٧٣٠/٦) (۱) قوله : "التخريج كذا في النسخة التى عندى والصحيح ههنا بدله : "الترجيح " كما نقل عن ابن الكمال في مواضع شتى وكما ذكره المصنف في حاشيته على الدر المختار 6 (۲) قوله : كأبي الحسن القدوري " كذا في النسخة التي بيدى، وكذا في نسخ القدوري، وهو غلط فاحش صدر من النساخ، والصحيح أبي الحسين، كما في "الكشف" ، و "الجواهر" ، و "الفوائد" ، و "وفيات الأعيان" . فليحفظ . واعلم أنه جعل القدورى وصاحب "الهداية " من أصحاب الترجيح، وقاضيخان من المجتهدين، مع تقدم القدوري على شمس الأئمة زمانًا، وكونه أعلى منه كعبا ، وأطول باعا، فكيف من قاضيخان . وأما صاحب الهداية : فهو المشار إليه في عصره، والمعقود عليه الخناصر في دهره ، وقد أقر له أهل عصره بالفضل والتقدم كالإمام فخر الدین قاضيخان وزين الدين ،وغيرهما، و قالوا : إنه فاق على أقرانه حتى على شيوخه في الفقه، فكيف ينزل عن شأنه عين قاضيخان؟ بل هو أحق منه بالاجتهاد وأثبت في أسبابه وألزم لأبوابه. فالإنصاف أن يعد من المجتهدين في المذهب، وهذا إلى العقل السليم أقرب . (مظ) وأجاب عنه بعض المحققين : بأن هذا الإشكال إنما نشأ مما يزعمه بعض الناس أن هذه الطبقات أقسام متباينة لا تجتمع في شخص واحد، فمن كان من أهل الترجيح لا يكون من أهل التخريج ، ومن كان من أهل التخريج لا يكون مجتهداً في المسائل. لكن الظاهر أن هذه الأقسام للوظائف لا للأشخاص، والمراد أن وظائف الفقهاء تنقسم إلى هذه الأقسام السبعة، ولا يستلزم من ذلك أن لا يكون الرجل يتولى جميع هذه الوظائف أو بعضها فى وقت واحد. وهذا كما أن العلماء ينتسبون إلى مفسر و محدث وفقيه ومتكلم، ولكن ربما يقع أن الرجل الواحد يصدق عليه جميع هذه الألقاب، فهو من حيث اشتغاله بالفقه فقيه، وبالقرآن مفسر، وبالحديث محدث، فكذلك يجوز أن يكون الرجل الواحد مجتهداً في المسائل، وأهلا للتخريج والترجيح في وقت واحد .
The fifth class: the class of those who perform takhrij (or tarjih) from among the muqallids, such as Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah, and their likes. Their function is to prefer some narrations over others. (2) Under the statement of the matn: 'And he has the lesser of the two shares, and they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: half of the two shares', its text: 'His saying: And they said: half of the two shares' meaning half of the total share of the male and female. Then know that this is the statement of al-Sha'bi, and since he was among the teachers of Abu Hanifa and had an ambiguous statement in this chapter, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad differed in his takhrij, so it is not their statement; because what is in al-Sirajiyyah is that the statement of Abu Hanifa is the statement of his companions, and it is the statement of the majority of the Companions, and the fatwa is upon it. (6/730) (1) His saying: 'al-takhrij' — thus in the copy I have, but the correct here is instead 'al-tarjih', as transmitted from Ibn al-Kamal in various places and as the author mentioned in his gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar. 6 (2) His saying: 'like Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri' — thus in the copy I have, and similarly in copies of al-Quduri, but it is a gross error from the scribes; the correct is Abu al-Husayn, as in al-Kashf, al-Jawahir, al-Fawa'id, and Wafayat al-A'yan. So let it be memorized. And know that he made al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah among the people of tarjih, and Qadi Khan among the mujtahids, despite al-Quduri being ahead of Shams al-A'imma in time, and being higher in rank and longer in reach — so how (could he be below) Qadi Khan? As for the author of al-Hidayah, he is the one referred to in his time, the one upon whom fingers are tied in his era, and his contemporaries acknowledged his excellence and precedence, such as Imam Fakhr al-Din Qadi Khan and Zayn al-Din and others, and they said: He surpassed his peers, even his teachers in fiqh, so how can his status be lowered compared to Qadi Khan? Rather, he is more deserving of ijtihad, more established in its means, and more committed to its doors. So fairness requires that he be counted among the mujtahids in the madhhab, and this is closer to sound reason. (Mz) And some verifiers answered: That this problem arises only from what some people claim that these classes are mutually exclusive divisions that cannot be combined in one person; so whoever is from the people of tarjih cannot be from the people of takhrij, and whoever is from the people of takhrij cannot be a mujtahid in issues. But the apparent is that these divisions are of functions, not persons; the meaning is that the functions of the jurists are divided into these seven categories, and it does not necessitate that a man cannot undertake all of these functions or some of them at one time. And this is like scholars being attributed as a mufassir, muhaddith, faqih, and mutakallim, but it may happen that one man is truthful in all these titles; he is, by virtue of his occupation with fiqh, a faqih; with the Quran, a mufassir; with hadith, a muhaddith. Similarly, it is permissible for one man to be a mujtahid in issues and also qualified for takhrij and tarjih at the same time.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage defines the fifth class of jurists according to Ibn Kamal Pasha's classification. The author begins by identifying them as 'ashab al-takhrij' (people of extrapolation) from among the muqallids, but immediately notes in the footnote that the correct term is 'ashab al-tarjih' (people of preference) based on Ibn al-Kamal's corrections. The text then gives an example of how these jurists work: they prefer some narrations over others, as illustrated by a discussion about the distribution of shares in inheritance between a male and female. The author clarifies that the statement attributed to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad is not actually theirs; it was derived from al-Sha'bi's ambiguous statement, and the correct ruling is Abu Hanifa's and the majority of Companions. The footnote then corrects a scribal error: 'Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri' should be 'Abu al-Husayn'. There follows a significant discussion about the relative ranks of scholars: the author of the footnote questions why al-Quduri and the author of al-Hidayah are classified as ashab al-tarjih while Qadi Khan is considered a mujtahid, when the former two are arguably more learned. The response concludes that the author of al-Hidayah should rightfully be counted among the mujtahidin, not merely a muqallid. A further note explains that the seven classes describe functions, not individuals; one scholar can fulfill multiple roles. This is analogous to a scholar being both a mufassir, muhaddith, faqih, and mutakallim. Thus, the classification is about what jurists do, not fixed labels.

Key Terms
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): Independent reasoning to derive rulings from the primary sources. In this context, it is a function that the author of al-Hidayah is argued to possess.
الطبقات (al-tabaqat): The seven classes of Hanafi jurists as defined by Ibn Kamal Pasha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the resolution to the apparent contradiction that the author of al-Hidayah is placed in the fifth class yet seems more learned than Qadi Khan?
A) The fifth class is actually higher than the seventh.
B) The classes are functions, not persons, so one can be both a mujtahid and ashab al-tarjih.
C) Qadi Khan was actually more learned than the author of al-Hidayah.
D) The author of al-Hidayah was incorrectly classified and should be in the seventh class.

Key Takeaway
The seven classes of Hanafi jurists describe functions, not persons; a single scholar can be a mujtahid and also perform tarjih.

The Sixth Layer: Muqallids Capable of Distinguishing Strong from Weak
Defining the sixth layer and distinguishing it from the fifth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the function of the sixth-layer muqallid and explain the difference between tamyiz and tarjih in Hanafi usul al-ifta.

Core Idea
Tamyiz is passive recognition of preponderance; tarjih is active ijtihad.

This lesson clarifies a key distinction in the Hanafi mufti hierarchy: the fifth layer performs tarjih (active weighing), while the sixth layer performs tamyiz (distinguishing between strong and weak based on established signs). A critique from al-Irshad challenges this distinction, and the author provides a nuanced response. Understanding this difference is essential for knowing whose opinions to rely upon in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sixth layer's function
State that the sixth layer is composed of muqallids who can distinguish (tamyiz) between stronger, strong, and weak narrations, and between Zahir al-Riwayah and rare narrations. They compile reliable texts like al-Kanz, al-Mukhtar, al-Wiqayah, and al-Majma'.
They do not perform tarjih themselves.
2
Understand the objection from al-Irshad
The critic argues that both the fifth and sixth layers seem to prefer some narrations over others, making them identical in meaning.
This objection is based on apparent similarity.
3
Analyze the author's first response
Tarjih involves actively correcting, preferring, and specifying the preponderant opinion—a type of ijtihad. Tamyiz is merely knowing what the people of tarjih have deemed preponderant, using their signs.
Tarjih is active; tamyiz is passive.
4
Analyze the second response
Tamyiz is more specific: it is confined to strength indicators. Tarjih is broader: it may consider convenience, timeliness, or other factors.
Tamyiz is a subset of tarjih in scope.
5
Apply to the mufti hierarchy
The mufti must know that the sixth layer's texts (like al-Kanz) are reliable and exclude weak narrations, but they do not handle conflicting corrections; the fifth layer's tarjih is needed for that.
This distinction guides which sources to use for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السادسة : طبقة المقلّدين القادرين على التمييز بين الأقوى والقوى والضعيف، وظاهر الرواية وظاهر المذهب والرواية النادرة، كأصحاب المتون المعتبرة كصاحب "الكنز"، وصاحب المختار"، وصاحب "الوقاية"، وصاحب "المجمع" . وشأنهم أن لا ينقلوا في كتبهم الأقوال المردودة، والروايات الضعيفة .
(۱) قوله : " القادرين على التمييز " اعترض في "الإرشاد" بأنه قال في الطبقة الخامسة: "إن شأنهم تفضيل بعض الروايات على بعض ... " ، وقال في الطبقة السادسة : "إنهم قادرون على التمييز بين القوى والضعيف . . . " فلم يكن فرق بين شأن الطبقتين في المعنى . (مظ)
ويمكن أن يجاب بأن الترجيح هو تصحيح الأقوال وتفضيل بعضها على بعض ، وتعيين الراجح من الأقوال عند اختلاف التصحيح، فهو نوع من التصرف يقتضى ضرباً من الاجتهاد، يتمكن به الإرشاد إلى القول المأخوذ به للعمل أو الإفتاء والقضاء، وأما التمييز فمعرفة ما رجحه أهل الترجيح مستمداً من علامات الترجيح وجمعها بين دفتين ولا دخل له في تصحيح الأقوال وتفضيلها والترجيح عند تعارض تصحيحها، وأجاب بعضهم بأن الثانى أخص ؛ فإنه مقصور على معرفة القوى من الضعيف بأماراته التي جعلها أهل الترجيح علمًا للراجح، وإدراجه في المتن، والأول أعم؛ فإن تفضيل بعض الروايات على البعض قد يكون لقوتها ، وقد يكون لوجوه أخرى ككونها أرفق للناس أو أوفق بالزمان وغير ذلك كما ستعرفه إن شاء الله تعالى .
The sixth layer: the layer of muqallids who are capable of distinguishing between the stronger, the strong, and the weak, and between the apparent transmission (Zahir al-Riwayah), the apparent madhhab, and the rare transmission (al-riwayah al-nadirah), such as the authors of reliable texts like the author of al-Kanz, the author of al-Mukhtar, the author of al-Wiqayah, and the author of al-Majma'. Their function is that they do not transmit in their books rejected opinions and weak narrations. (1) His statement: 'capable of distinguishing' – it was objected in al-Irshad that he said regarding the fifth layer: 'Their function is to prefer some narrations over others...' and he said regarding the sixth layer: 'They are capable of distinguishing between the strong and the weak...' So there is no difference between the functions of the two layers in meaning. (Mazhar) And it can be answered that tarjih (weighing) is the correction of opinions and preferring some over others, and specifying the preponderant opinion when there is difference in correction; it is a type of action requiring a kind of ijtihad, by which one can guide to the opinion adopted for practice, issuing fatwa, or judgment. As for tamyiz (distinguishing), it is knowing what the people of tarjih have deemed preponderant, derived from the signs of tarjih and gathering them between two covers; it has no role in correcting opinions and preferring them, nor in weighing when their corrections conflict. And some answered that the second [i.e., tamyiz] is more specific, for it is confined to knowing the strong from the weak by its indicators which the people of tarjih have made a sign for the preponderant, and inserting it into the text, while the first [i.e., tarjih] is more general, for preferring some narrations over others may be due to their strength or due to other reasons such as being more convenient for people or more suitable for the time, and other than that, as you will come to know, Allah willing.
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage defines the sixth layer in the hierarchy of muqallids (those who follow the madhhab) according to Hanafi usul al-ifta. The sixth layer comprises those who can distinguish between different levels of strength in narrations and rulings (stronger, strong, weak) and between the authoritative transmissions (Zahir al-Riwayah) and rare ones, but they do not perform tarjih (weighing) themselves. They compile reliable texts (like al-Kanz, al-Mukhtar, al-Wiqayah, al-Majma') and exclude rejected opinions. A critique from al-Irshad argues that the sixth layer's function (tamyiz) is essentially the same as the fifth layer's function (tarjih), since both involve preferring some narrations over others. The author responds by distinguishing between tarjih (an active ijtihad process of correcting and preferring opinions) and tamyiz (simply knowing what the people of tarjih have already deemed preponderant). Tamyiz is merely recognizing the preponderant based on established signs; it does not involve the act of weighing itself. Another response notes that tamyiz is more specific (confined to strength indicators), while tarjih is broader (it may consider other factors like convenience or timeliness). Thus, the layers are distinct in their capacity and function.

Key Terms
التمييز (al-tamyiz): Distinguishing between strong and weak narrations/rulings based on signs established by the people of tarjih, without performing the weighing process itself.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The process of weighing and preferring one opinion or narration over another, involving correction and ijtihad.
المقلّدون (al-muqallidun): Those who follow the madhhab without being able to derive rulings independently; they operate within the framework of the school's established opinions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the distinguishing feature of the sixth layer compared to the fifth layer?
A) The sixth layer can perform tarjih with full ijtihad
B) The sixth layer only transmits narrations without any selection
C) The sixth layer can distinguish between strong and weak but does not perform active tarjih
D) The sixth layer includes only authors of later fatwa collections

Key Takeaway
The sixth-layer muqallid performs tamyiz—passive recognition of preponderant narrations—while the fifth-layer muqallid performs tarjih—active ijtihad that may consider broader factors beyond textual strength.

The Seventh Layer: Muqallids Who Cannot Distinguish – A Warning
Defining the seventh layer and the prohibition on following such muqallids.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the characteristics of the seventh layer of muqallids and state the ruling on following them according to the Hanafi rasm al-mufti.

Core Idea
Following a muqallid who cannot distinguish sound from unsound rulings is severely prohibited — woe to whoever follows them.

In this passage, the author defines the lowest category of muqallids: those who lack even the basic ability to differentiate between valid and invalid rulings. They collect fatwas indiscriminately, like one gathering firewood at night. The text issues an emphatic warning against relying on such individuals for guidance, and also includes a discussion about the validity of the classification itself, as well as an important reminder for muftis and judges to be thorough and avoid haste.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seventh layer's defining traits
Read the definition: these muqallids cannot distinguish between sound (samin) and unsound (ghathth) rulings, nor right from left. They collect all they find like a nighttime firewood gatherer (hatibu layl).
These traits indicate complete lack of discernment.
2
Understand the severity of the warning
The text says 'الويل لمن قلدهم كل الويل' (woe, all woe to whoever follows them). This is a strong prohibition against taking fatwa from such individuals.
In fiqh, such language indicates haram.
3
Examine the dispute about the seven-layer classification
Some scholars (as noted in the margin) criticize al-Taymi's classification as arbitrary and erroneous. The author claims to have answered these objections. Be aware that the classification itself is not universally accepted, but the warning against unqualified muqallids is agreed upon.
The core ruling remains even if the classification is disputed.
4
Connect to mufti adab from al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah
The excerpt emphasizes that muftis and judges must be thorough (tathabbut), avoid haste (mujazafah), and fear fabricating against Allah. This reinforces the gravity of issuing fatwa without proper knowledge.
The seventh layer represents the extreme opposite of these qualities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السابعة : طبقة المقلدين (۱) الذين لا يقدرون على ما ذكر، ولا يفرقون بين الغث (۲) والسمين ، ولا يميزون الشمال من اليمين، بل يجمعون ما يجدون كحاطب ليل، فالويل لمن قلدهم كل الويل . انتهى مع حذف شيء يسير . وستأتى بقية الكلام في ذلك . وفي آخر الفتاوى الخيرية (۳) : " ولا شك أن معرفة راجح المختلف فيه من مرجوحه ومراتبه قوة وضعفًا - هو نهاية آمال المشمرين في تحصيل العلم. فالمفروض على المفتى والقاضي التثبت في الجواب وعدم المجازفة (٤) فيها؛ خوفًا من الافتراء على الله تعالى بتحريم حلال وضده. ويحرم اتباع الهوى والتشهى والميل إلى المال الذى هو الداهية (٥) الكبرى، والمصيبة العظمى ؛ فإن ذلك أمر عظيم لا يتجاسر عليه إلا كل جاهل شقى " . اهـ .
(۱) قوله : "السابعة : طبقة المقلدين " قال بعض الأفاضل : "كذا ذكر التيمي المراتب السبع في طبقاته، وقال: هو تقسيم حسن جدا مع أنه بعيد جدا عن الصحة فضلا عن الحسن، فإنه تحكم محض ، ولا سلف له في هذه الدعوى، وإن تابعه عليها من جاء بعده وحذا حذوه من غير دليل يدل على ذلك. وعلى فرض تسليم أن الفقهاء والمتفقهة على هذه المراتب السبع، لا نسلم الخطأ الفاحش الذي وقع في تعيين رجال الطبقات، وترتيبهم على هذه الدرجات . ثم بين ذلك الخطأ، وذكر مثل ما ذكرنا فيما قبل . (مظ) وقد أشبعناك بجوابه فلتكن منه على بصيرة .
(۲) قوله : "الغث بالفتح : المهزول، والسمين ضده. (مظ) والمراد به الجيد والردىء من الكلام .
(۳) قوله : " في آخر الفتاوى الخيرية " أي في مسائل شتى . (مظ)
(٤) قوله : "المجازفة يقال : جازف فى كلامه أى تكلّم بلا قانون وبدون تبصر . (مظ) وقوله : "فيهما " أي في الإفتاء والقضاء .
(٥) قوله : "الداهية " أى الأمر المنكر، والمصيبة، والأمر العظيم. (مظ)
The seventh layer: the layer of muqallids (1) who are not capable of what was mentioned [above], and they do not distinguish between the lean (2) and the fat, nor do they differentiate right from left; rather they collect whatever they find like a nighttime gatherer (of firewood). So woe, all woe to whoever follows them. End, with the omission of a little. And the rest of the discussion will come regarding that. And in the end of al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah (3): 'There is no doubt that knowing the preponderant from the non-preponderant in matters of disagreement, and their levels in strength and weakness, is the ultimate aspiration of those who strive in acquiring knowledge. So it is obligatory upon the mufti and the judge to be thorough in the answer and not to be hasty (4) therein, for fear of fabricating against Allah Almighty by declaring lawful as unlawful and vice versa. And it is forbidden to follow desire and caprice and inclination toward wealth, which is the great calamity (5) and the immense disaster; for that is a grave matter, which none dares except every ignorant wretch.' End.
(1) His statement: 'The seventh layer: the layer of muqallids' – Some scholars said: 'Thus al-Taymi mentioned the seven categories in his Tabaqat, and said: It is a very good classification, although it is very far from correctness, let alone goodness, for it is pure arbitrary judgment, and he has no predecessor in this claim, and those who came after him followed him and followed his example without evidence indicating that. And assuming we accept that the fuqaha and those studying fiqh are upon these seven categories, we do not accept the gross error that occurred in specifying the men of these layers and arranging them in these ranks. Then he explained that error and mentioned similar to what we mentioned before.' (Mazhar) And we have sufficiently answered him, so be aware of it.
(2) His statement: 'al-ghathth (lean) with a fatha means emaciated, and al-samin (fat) is its opposite. (Mazhar) The intended meaning is the good and bad of speech.
(3) His statement: 'in the end of al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah' meaning in miscellaneous issues. (Mazhar)
(4) His statement: 'al-mujazafah' – they say: he spoke with mujazafah i.e. he spoke without law and without insight. (Mazhar) And his statement: 'fihima' i.e. in issuing fatwa and judgment.
(5) His statement: 'al-dahiyah' means the reprehensible matter, the calamity, and the great matter. (Mazhar)
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage defines the seventh and lowest layer in the hierarchy of muqallids. These individuals lack even the ability to distinguish between sound and unsound rulings (likened to distinguishing lean from fat meat, or right from left). They collect narrations indiscriminately, like one who gathers firewood at night without knowing what he picks up. The text issues a severe warning: 'woe to whoever follows them.' This stark warning underscores the danger of relying on such unqualified persons for fatwa. The marginal notes add a critical discussion about the entire classification system itself, with some scholars objecting that al-Taymi's seven-layer scheme is arbitrary and unsupported. However, the author dismisses this objection. The passage concludes with an excerpt from al-Fatawa al-Khayriyyah emphasizing the heavy responsibility of muftis and judges: they must be thorough, avoid hastiness, guard against fabricating rulings, and abstain from following desires or seeking wealth, as such conduct leads to great sin.

Key Terms
الغث والسمين (al-ghathth wa al-samin): Literally 'lean and fat'; metaphorically refers to the good and bad, sound and unsound in speech or rulings.
حاطب ليل (hatibu layl): One who gathers firewood at night, collecting indiscriminately without discernment; used to describe someone who gathers rulings without discrimination.
المجازفة (al-mujazafah): Hasty, careless speech or action without proper deliberation or legal framework.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on following a muqallid from the seventh layer?
A) It is permissible but not recommended
B) It is obligatory to follow them in matters of necessity
C) It is severely warned against: woe to whoever follows them
D) It is allowed only if they have a written text

Key Takeaway
A muqallid who cannot distinguish between sound and unsound rulings must not be followed; seeking fatwa from such a person is prohibited.

The Seventh Level of Muqallideen: Between Classification and Criticism
Description and criticism of the lowest level of muqallideen

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the criticism of the seven-level classification of jurists and articulate the Hanafi response defending its pedagogical utility.

Core Idea
Blind following without discernment is not scholarship, but classification of jurists is a useful pedagogical tool despite scholarly criticism.

This passage from Sharh Uqood Rasm al-Mufti describes the lowest level of muqallideen (blind followers) who collect rulings indiscriminately, like a night wood-gatherer. Then it presents a strong criticism that the entire seven-level classification is arbitrary and historically unsupported. The commentary responds by affirming that a sufficient answer has been given, inviting us to understand the classification's value while acknowledging the debate. This lesson will help you navigate the controversy and its implications for fatwa authority.

Guided Path
1
Identify the seventh level description
Read the first part of the passage. What is the defining characteristic of the seventh level? They cannot distinguish between sound and unsound opinions, like a night wood-gatherer.
The metaphors 'lean and fat' and 'left from right' emphasize total lack of discernment.
2
Summarize the criticism
Some virtuous scholars (al-afadil) criticize al-Taymi's classification as arbitrary (tahakkum mahd), with no precedent, and with errors in assigning specific scholars to ranks.
The critic challenges both the division itself and its application to historical figures.
3
Identify the Hanafi response
The commentary says 'We have sufficiently answered you' (wa qad ashba'nak bijawabihi), implying the criticism has been addressed elsewhere. The classification is upheld as useful despite the critiques.
The response is not expanded here; the reader is directed to be on insight (bastira).
4
Determine practical impact on fatwa authority
If the classification is accepted, it establishes a clear hierarchy for whose fatwa is authoritative. If rejected, all muqallideen are equally untrustworthy, but the Hanafi school relies on the classification.
The mufta bihi position is to use the classification as a pedagogical tool, not as a rigid historical claim.
5
Apply to modern mufti training
A mufti today must learn to distinguish reliable from unreliable fatwas, akin to the first level of mujtahids. The seventh level warns against issuing fatwas without proper training.
This passage guards against the common misunderstanding that memorization of many texts suffices for fatwa.

The seventh level: The level of the muqallideen (blind followers) who are not capable of what was mentioned, and they do not differentiate between the lean and the fat, and they do not distinguish left from right, but rather they collect whatever they find like a night wood-gatherer. So woe to whoever follows them, total woe. Ended with the omission of something small. The rest of the speech on that will come. (1) His saying: 'The seventh: the level of the muqallideen' – some virtuous ones said: 'Thus al-Taymi mentioned the seven ranks in his strata, and he said: it is a very good division, although it is very far from correctness, let alone goodness, for it is pure arbitrariness, and he has no predecessor in this claim, even if those who came after him followed him and imitated him without evidence indicating that. And assuming that the jurists and students of jurisprudence are upon these seven ranks, we do not accept the egregious error that occurred in determining the men of the ranks and arranging them in these degrees. Then he explained that error and mentioned similar to what we mentioned before. (mazhar) And we have sufficiently answered you with his response, so be upon insight from it. (2) His saying: 'al-ghuthth' with fathah: the thin, and al-sameen is its opposite. (mazhar) And what is meant by it is the good and bad of speech.'

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the adab (etiquette) of the mufti regarding the classification of jurists. It describes the seventh and lowest level: those who blindly quote rulings without any ability to distinguish between sound and weak opinions, likened to a person gathering firewood at night without discernment. The author then quotes a criticism from 'some virtuous ones' challenging the validity of this seven-tier classification as arbitrary and unsupported by earlier authorities. The criticism points out errors in assigning specific scholars to ranks. The commentary (mazhar) affirms that a sufficient response has been given, advising the reader to be on clear insight. This passage guards against the common misunderstanding that any level of scholarship is acceptable for issuing fatwas; rather, ignorance and blind following are dangerous.

Key Terms
المقلدين (al-muqallideen): Those who blindly follow the opinions of others without knowledge or ability to differentiate.
الغث والسمين (al-ghuthth wa al-sameen): Metaphor for sound and unsound opinions; literally lean and fat.
حاطب ليل (hatib layl): One who gathers firewood at night, metaphor for collecting anything without discerning quality.

Books Not Permissible for Fatwa and the Six Defects
Rule about books not permissible for fatwa with six defects and Ibn Nujaym's principles

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six aspects that disqualify a book for fatwa and apply the two principles of Ibn Nujaym to evaluate a source.

Core Idea
Not every fiqh book is reliable for fatwa—six defects must be checked, and true understanding requires mastering principles, not just referencing texts.

This lesson introduces a critical rule for muftis: not all books are permissible for issuing fatwa. The author lists six defects that render a book unreliable and emphasizes that mere reference is insufficient. Ibn Nujaym’s two principles provide the deeper foundation: understanding underlying restrictions and the rational basis of rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six defects
From the text, list the six aspects that disqualify a book: lack of concern for correctness, extreme brevity, preference for non-rajih opinions, transmitting weak rulings, ignorance of the author's status, and ignorance of what is attributed to him.
These are specific criteria used in the Hanafi school to evaluate fiqh works.
2
Explain why thiqah is lacking
Understand that fiqh is not obtained by mere reference to a book; one must have training and understanding of principles. The author argues that often a ruling in one book may be superseded by another.
Thiqah refers to trustworthiness; without it, a book cannot be used for fatwa.
3
Apply Ibn Nujaym's first principle
Know that jurists' absolute expressions are generally restricted by unstated conditions. Only a student with sound understanding and practice in usul and furu' can grasp these restrictions.
This guards against taking absolute statements at face value.
4
Apply Ibn Nujaym's second principle
Recognize that rulings are based on underlying principles (asl) and are rationally motivated. Without knowing the basis, one will make errors.
Understanding the 'illah (effective cause) is key to correct application.
5
Evaluate a hypothetical book
Given a book, check it against the six defects and Ibn Nujaym's principles. For example, a concise fatwa collection with no mention of the author's credentials would fail due to defect 4 (ignorance of author's status).
This is a practical step for a mufti in training.

Source Text

الكتب التي لا يجوز الإفتاء بها
مطلب
الكتب التي لا يجوز
الإفتاء بها ، ووجوهه ستة سنة (١)
قلت : فحيث علمت وجوب اتباع الراجح من الأقوال، وحال المرجح
له (۲) ، تعلم أنه لا ثقة (۳) بما يفتى به أكثر أهل زماننا بمجرد مراجعه (4) کتاب من
(۱) قوله : ووجوهه ستة هي: عدم الاهتمام بالتصحيح، وشدة الإيجاز في التعبير، وترجيح خلاف الراجح ، ونقل الأقوال الضعيفة وعدم الاطلاع على حال المؤلف، وعدم علم المنقول عنه . .
(۲) قوله : "وحال المرجح له " عطف على مفعول "علمت"، والضمير المجرور راجع إلى "الراجح " ، أى حيث علمت حال من يرجح الراجح .
(۳) قوله : "لا ثقة" لأن الفقه لا يحصل بمجرد القدرة على مراجعة المسألة من مظانها، ولو كان كذلك لكان الفقه أسهل شيء، ولما احتاج إلى التفقه على أستاذ ماهر وفكر ثاقب، فكثيراً ما تذكر المسألة في كتاب ويكون ما في كتاب آخر هو الصحيح
والصواب، وقد تطلق في بعض المواضع عن بعض قيودها، وتقيد في موضع . ولهذا قال ابن نجيم: إن فهم المسائل على التحقيق يحتاج إلى معرفة أصلين : :أحدهما أن إطلاقات الفقهاء في الغالب مقيدة بقيود يعرفها صاحب الفهم المستقيم الممارس للأصول والفروع ، وأنهم يسكتون عنها اعتمادا على صحة فهم الطالب. والثاني : أن هذه المسائل اجتهادية معقولة المعنى لا يعرف الحكم فيها على الوجه التام إلا بمعرفة وجه الحكم الذى تبنى عليه، وتفرع عنه، وإلا فتشتبه المسائل على الطالب، ويحار ذهنه فيها ; لعدم معرفة المبنى، ومن جهل ما ذكرنا حار في الخطأ والغلط . (مظ) (٤) قوله بمجرد مراجعة بل الواجب عليهم أن يجتهدوا في تحقيق المسائل والرجوع إلى الكتب المعتبرة، فلا يعتمدوا على كل كتاب لا سيما الفتاوى التي هي
The books that it is not permissible to issue fatwa from. Section: The books that it is not permissible to issue fatwa from, and its aspects are six (1). I say: Since you have known the obligation of following the preponderant (rajih) of the statements, and the condition of the one who gives preponderance to it (2), you know that there is no trust (3) in what most of the people of our time issue fatwa with by mere reference to a book from... (1) His saying: 'and its aspects are six': lack of concern for correctness, extreme brevity in expression, preferring contrary to the rajih, transmitting weak statements, lack of knowledge of the author's status, and lack of knowledge of what is transmitted from him. (2) His saying: 'and the condition of the one who gives preponderance to it' is an apposition to the object of 'you know', and the attached pronoun refers back to 'al-rajih', i.e., when you know the condition of the one who gives preponderance to the rajih. (3) His saying: 'no trust' because fiqh is not obtained by mere ability to review the issue from its sources; if that were the case, fiqh would be the easiest thing, and there would be no need to study under a skilled teacher and have sharp thought. Often an issue is mentioned in one book while what is in another book is correct and sound, and it may be stated in some places without some of its restrictions, and restricted in another. For this reason, Ibn Nujaym said: Understanding issues accurately requires knowledge of two principles: one is that the absolute expressions of the jurists are generally restricted by restrictions known to the person of sound understanding who has practiced the principles and branches, and they remain silent about them relying on the correct understanding of the student. The second: that these issues are ijtihad-based with reasonable meanings; the ruling is not known fully except by knowing the basis of the ruling upon which it is built and from which it is derived; otherwise issues become confusing to the student and his mind becomes perplexed due to lack of knowledge of the basis. And whoever is ignorant of what we mentioned will flounder in error and mistake. (mazhar) (4) His saying: 'by mere reference' – rather it is obligatory upon them to strive in investigating the issues and refer to the reliable books, so they should not rely on every book, especially the fatwas that are...
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti (rule) introducing the topic of books from which fatwa is not permissible. It outlines six aspects (وجوه) that render a book unreliable: lack of concern for correctness, extreme brevity, preference for non-rajih opinions, transmission of weak rulings, ignorance of the author's status, and ignorance of what is attributed to him. The author then explains why mere reference to any book is insufficient: fiqh requires deep understanding, not just the ability to locate a ruling. He quotes Ibn Nujaym who states that mastering fiqh requires knowing that jurists' absolute expressions are often qualified by unstated conditions, and that rulings are based on underlying principles (asl) that must be understood. Without this, one will make errors. This guards against the common misunderstanding that any fatwa collection can be used blindly by an untrained person.

Key Terms
الكتب التي لا يجوز الإفتاء بها (al-kutub allati la yajuz al-ifta' biha): Books that are not reliable for issuing fatwas due to one or more of the six identified defects.
الوجوه الستة (al-wujuh al-sittah): The six aspects or reasons that disqualify a book from being used for fatwa.
الثقة (al-thiqah): Trustworthiness of a book or its rulings; absence of thiqah means the book cannot be relied upon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Because most people do not have access to books.
D) Because modern books are not written in Arabic.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must vet any source book against the six defects and ensure understanding of underlying principles before using it for fatwa.

Books Not Permissible for Fatwa and Their Conditions
Listing prohibited fatwa sources and their conditional permissibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify later Hanafi works impermissible for direct fatwa and explain the condition under which they may be used.

Core Idea
Not all Hanafi books are reliable for fatwa; later concise works may contain errors and require expert verification.

A mufti must know which sources are authoritative. This passage from 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti warns against using certain later works for fatwa due to conciseness and inaccuracies, but also gives a condition when they may be consulted.

Guided Path
1
Recognize two categories
The passage divides problematic books into later concise works (kutub muta'akhira, especially ghayr al-muharrar) and strange works (ghariba). Understand the distinction.
'Ghayr al-muharrar' means unclear due to extreme brevity.
2
Identify specific books
List the mentioned books: Sharh al-Niqaya, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, Mulla Miskin's Sharh al-Kanz, al-Qahhistani, and many others listed in the footnotes.
These are examples; the rule applies to similar works.
3
Understand reasons for prohibition
The books are problematic due to extreme conciseness (like riddles), omissions in transmission, and giving precedence to weak or even non-Hanafi views.
The main issue is lack of clarity and potential for error.
4
Note the exception
An expert mufti may use these books if he can sift the strong (rajih) from the weak (marjuh), like gathering dry and wet from a desert.
The mufti must have deep knowledge of the madhhab to do this.
5
Apply the rule
When encountering a fatwa from al-Durr al-Mukhtar, for example, understand that it must be verified against earlier reliable sources (mutun and shuruh).
Direct reliance is not allowed.

الكتب التي لا يجوز الإفتاء بها
شرح عقود رسم المفتی الكتب المتأخرة، خصوصا غير المحررة (۱) شرح النقاية " للقهستاني، و الدر المختار" ، و الأشباه والنظائر ونحوها؛ فإنها لشدة الاختصار والإيجاز كادت تلحق بالألغاز ، مع ما اشتملت عليه من السقط في النقل في مواضع كثيرة ، وترجيح ما هو خلاف الراجح، بل ترجیح ما هو مذهب الغير، مما لم يقل به أحد من أهل المذهب .
ورأيت في أوائل شرح الأشباه للعلامة محمد هبة الله قال : "ومن الكتب الغريبة : "ملا مسكين شرح الكنز ، و القهستاني ؛ لعدم الاطلاع على حال مؤلفيهما، أو لنقل الأقوال الضعيفة كصاحب القنية" ، أو لاختصار كـ الدر المختار للحصكفى ، و "النهر " و "العيني " شرح الكنز .
مطلب
متى يجوز الإفتاء من هذه الكتب
(۲)
قال شيخنا صالح الجينيني : "إنه لا يجوز الإفتاء من هذه الكتب، إلا
كالصحارى جامعة للرطب واليابس، والقوى والضعيف، والراجح والمرجوح قال في حواشي الأشباه للحموي نقلا عن "الفوائد الزينية " : "لا تجوز الفتوى من التصانيف غير المشهورة . (مظ)
(۱) قوله : "غير المحرر " أى غير الواضحة ؛ لشدة الإيجاز في التعبير، فلا يجوز الإفتاء بها ما لم يستعن بالشروح والحواشي .
(۲) قوله : "لا يجوز الإفتاء " وكذا لا يجوز من المحيط البرهاني"، و "السراج الوهاج" ، و "الأحكام لفخر الدين الرومي، و كنز العباد مطالب المؤمنين " ، و خزانة الروايات"، و "الفتاوى الصوفية"، و "فتاوى الطوري " ، و " فتاوى ابن نجيم"، و "فتاوى إبراهيم شاهي"، و "خلاصة الكيداني"، و "الحاوي"، و "المجتبى شرح مختصر القدورى " ، و "زاد الأئمة" وغير ذلك . (مظ)
The books from which it is not permissible to issue fatwa: The commentary of 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti: The later books, especially those that are not well-edited (1) such as Sharh al-Niqaya by al-Qahhistani, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, and similar works; for due to extreme conciseness and brevity they almost become riddles, along with what they contain of omissions in transmission in many places, and giving precedence to what is contrary to the preponderant view, even giving precedence to the position of others, which no one from the school has held. I saw in the beginning of Sharh al-Ashbah by Allamah Muhammad Hibbatullah that he said: 'Among the strange books are: Mulla Miskin's Sharh al-Kanz, and al-Qahhistani; due to lack of knowledge of the condition of their authors, or due to quoting weak opinions like the author of al-Qunyah, or due to conciseness like al-Durr al-Mukhtar by al-Haskafi, and al-Nahr, and al-'Ayni's Sharh al-Kanz.' Section: When is it permissible to issue fatwa from these books? (2) Our teacher Salih al-Jinini said: 'It is not permissible to issue fatwa from these books except like a desert that gathers wet and dry, strong and weak, preponderant and preponderated.' In Hawashi al-Ashbah by al-Hamawi, quoting from al-Fawa'id al-Zainiyyah: 'Fatwa is not permissible from unfamiliar works.' (Mazhar). (1) His statement: 'non-muharrar' means unclear; due to extreme conciseness in expression, so fatwa is not permissible from them unless one uses commentaries and marginal notes. (2) His statement: 'it is not permissible to issue fatwa' – likewise it is not permissible from al-Muhit al-Burhani, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, al-Ahkam li Fakhr al-Din al-Rumi, Kanz al-'Ibad Matalib al-Mu'minin, Khizanat al-Riwayat, al-Fatawa al-Sufiyyah, Fatawa al-Turi, Fatawa Ibn Nujaym, Fatawa Ibrahim Shahi, Khulasat al-Kidani, al-Hawi, al-Mujtaba Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri, Zad al-A'immah, and others. (Mazhar).
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a rasm al-mufti rule concerning the permissibility of issuing fatwa from certain books. The author identifies two categories of problematic books: (1) later works (kutub muta'akhira) that are extremely concise and may contain errors or weak positions, such as Sharh al-Niqaya, al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir; (2) 'strange books' (ghariba) like Mulla Miskin's commentary and al-Qahhistani, which may have weak authors or weak opinions. A key distinction is that some books are 'ghayr muharrar' (unclear/unedited), meaning their brevity makes them unreliable without reference to commentaries (shuruh) and marginal notes (hawashi). The rule is that fatwa from these books is not permissible unless one is an expert who can sift the strong from the weak, like one who gathers from a desert. The footnotes list additional works from which fatwa is also not allowed, including al-Muhit al-Burhani, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and Fatawa Ibn Nujaym. The underlying principle is that a mufti must rely on well-established, clear sources that represent the preponderant (rajih) view of the Hanafi school, not on obscure or overly concise works that may misrepresent the madhhab.

Key Terms
غير المحرر (ghayr al-muharrar): Unclear or not properly edited; refers to books with extreme conciseness that may cause confusion.
الكتب المتأخرة (al-kutub al-muta'akhira): Later works of the Hanafi school that are often concise and may contain omissions or weak rulings.
الكتب غير المشهورة (al-kutub ghayr al-mashhura): Unfamous or obscure books that are not widely recognized in the madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why are books like al-Durr al-Mukhtar not permissible for direct fatwa?
A) They contain many weak and erroneous rulings.
B) They are too concise and unclear, requiring reference to commentaries.
C) They are not well-known in the Hanafi school.
D) They are only for teaching, not fatwa.

Key Takeaway
Fatwa from later concise Hanafi works is not permissible unless the mufti is an expert who can distinguish the sound from the weak.

Necessity of Returning to Original Sources for Fatwa
Rasm al-mufti rule emphasizing verification of original sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the principle of verifying original sources (al-ma'khadh al-asli) to identify propagated errors in fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti must trace every ruling to its original source; a widely repeated error remains an error.

A mufti often encounters a ruling cited in numerous later compilations. The natural tendency is to assume its reliability. However, this lesson warns that an error introduced by an early author can be copied without correction by many successors. The mufti’s duty is to trace back to the foundational texts of the Hanafi madhhab, such as Zahir al-Riwayah, to ensure the fatwa's authenticity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Principle
Read the opening: 'لا بد من المراجعة إلى المأخذ الأصلى'. Recognize that the mufti must return to the original source and not rely on secondary compilations.
The term 'مأخذ أصلى' refers to the primary texts like al-Mabsut or al-Jami' al-Saghir.
2
Understand the Warning about Error Propagation
The text warns that a single error by the first originator can be transmitted through dozens of later books. Note the phrase 'يتفق نقل قول في نحو عشرين كتاباً من كتب المتأخرين، ويكون القول خطأ'.
This does not impugn the later scholars; it highlights the human tendency to copy without verification.
3
Analyze the Given Examples
Examine the two examples: (1) issues of valid suspension in contracts, noted by Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq; (2) hiring for bare Quran recitation. In both cases, an initial error spread across many works.
These examples show that even a well-known ruling may be false if its chain is not verified.
4
Apply the Principle of 'Uhda (Responsibility)
Understand that the transmitter bears the 'uhda (guarantee) of accuracy. The mufti must check the chain of transmission back to the original source to ensure the ruling's correctness.
The 'uhda assigns responsibility; if the chain is broken or erroneous, the ruling is invalid.

The importance of reviewing the original source: When one knows from whom it is transmitted, and examines its sources. This is how I heard from him, and he is a well-known scholar in fiqh, and the responsibility is upon him. End. Section: It is necessary to refer to the original source and not to rely on the secondary source. I say: It may happen that a statement is transmitted in about twenty books of later authors, and that statement is an error made by the first originator, then the one after him comes and transmits it from him, (1) and thus they transmit from one another. 1. As occurred in some issues of what is valid to suspend and what is not, as pointed out by Allamah Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. 2. Among that (3) is the issue of hiring for bare recitation of the Quran, for it occurred... And his statement: 'and the responsibility is upon him' – it is said: the responsibility of the report is on its transmitter, i.e., guarantee of its truthfulness is upon him. (1) His statement: 'the first originator made an error' – the cause of error may be a slip of the pen, or confusing one ruling with another, or the like, and all that does not diminish their status at all, nor does it necessitate lack of trust in them absolutely; because there is no blame on them, and most often the error is from one person, then the one after him follows him, as the author mentioned its parallels. (Mazhar) (2) His statement: 'In al-Bahr al-Ra'iq' – the author of al-Bahr said in the chapter of miscellaneous issues from the book of sales, when mentioning issues that are valid to suspend and those that are not: 'It often happens that an author mentions something erroneously in his book, then later scholars come after him and transmit that expression without change or warning, so the transmitters become many, while the original one is mistaken, as occurred in this place.' (6/308) (3) His statement: 'Among that' – i.e., among what happens that a statement is transmitted in twenty books and the statement is erroneous.
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage expands on the rasm al-mufti principle that a mufti must trace rulings back to their original sources (ma'khadh asli) and not rely solely on secondary sources (ma'khadh thanawi). The author emphasizes that even if a ruling appears in many later books, it may be based on an initial error. Two concrete examples are given: (1) issues of what can be suspended in contracts, as noted by Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, where a mistake by one author was copied by many; (2) the issue of hiring for bare Quran recitation (i.e., recitation without other conditions), which also became widely transmitted despite the original error. The footnotes explain that such errors do not discredit the scholars, as they are human, but the mufti must verify. The key term 'al-'uhda' (responsibility) indicates that the transmitter bears the burden of accuracy. The lesson is a warning against blind acceptance of widely repeated rulings; a mufti must consult the foundational texts (asl) of the madhhab, such as Zahir al-Riwayah, before issuing fatwa.

Key Terms
المأخذ الأصلى (al-ma'khadh al-asli): The original source or primary reference from which a ruling is taken.
العهدة (al-'uhda): Responsibility for the correctness of a report; the guarantor of its authenticity.
المأخذ الثانوى (al-ma'khadh al-thaanawi): Secondary source that relies on primary sources but may contain errors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What does the example of the issue of hiring for Quran recitation illustrate?
A) That some rulings are only found in later books.
B) That an error can be propagated across many books if the original source was mistaken.
C) That the Hanafi school prohibits hiring for Quran recitation.
D) That later scholars always correct earlier mistakes.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must never rely solely on the number of books quoting a ruling; he must trace it to the original source.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
The Obligation to Verify Original Sources
Warning against relying on later texts without verifying original sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rasm al-mufti principle that a transmitted fatwa must be verified against its original source (al-makhadhal al-asli) and distinguish the specific exception for teaching Quran from the general rule prohibiting hiring for acts of worship.

Core Idea
A mufti must trace every ruling to its original source — later texts may corrupt the exception into a rule.

This passage from Ibn Abidin's Rasm al-Mufti warns against blindly accepting later fatwas without checking the original sources. It exposes a common error: the blanket permission to hire for acts of worship, which actually was only a specific concession for teaching the Quran. As a mufti, you must be a researcher (muhaqqiq), not a mere transmitter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule
State the core methodological lesson: the mufti must refer to the original source (makhadhal asli) before transmitting any fatwa.
This is the foundation of the rasm al-mufti tradition.
2
Analyze the hiring error
Examine how later scholars mistakenly generalized the permissibility of hiring for teaching Quran to all acts of worship. Identify the confusion between 'tilawah' (recitation) and teaching.
The error arose because the original fatwa was specific, but later texts quoted it absolutely.
3
Trace the trusts error
Investigate the second example: Qadikhan's transmission that trusts become guaranteed upon death except in three cases. Find out how al-Bahr corrected it to ten exceptions.
The error originated from al-Natafi and was perpetuated without verification.
4
Synthesize the principle
Explain why the later fatwa on teaching Quran is an istihsan (juristic preference) based on necessity, not a revocation of the original ruling. Contrast the original hukm with the mufta bihi exception.
The exception is conditional and does not extend to other acts of worship.
5
Apply to a new case
Given a fatwa in a later Hanafi text, outline the steps you would take to verify it: locate the original source, check for conditions, identify if it is a rukhsah, and confirm its scope.
This step integrates the lesson into practical mufti work.
