(۲) قوله : "فأفتوا بصحته" قال المرغيناني وبعض مشايخنا : "استحسنوا الاستئجار على تعليم القرآن اليوم ؛ لظهور التواني في الأمور الدينية، ففى الامتناع تضييع حفظ القرآن وعليه الفتوى . ، وقال في متن "الكنز" بعد ذكره عدم الجواز فيما مر : " والفتوى اليوم على جواز الاستئجار على تعليم القرآن" ، وهكذا في غير كتاب من الكتب المعتمدة في المذهب، وفى "الخلاصة" : " ولا بأس بأخذ الأجرة بتعليم القرآن في زماننا " . قال الفقيه أبو الليث : كنت أفتى بثلاثة فرجعت عنها : أفتى أن لا يحلّ أخذ الأجرة على تعليم القرآن، وأنه لا ينبغي للعالم أن يدخل على السلطان، وأنه لا ينبغي أن يخرج إلى الرستاق، فرجعت عن الكل تحرزاً من ضياع القرآن، ولحاجة الخلق ولجهل أهل الرستاق".
وقال قاضيخان : " ومشايخ بلخ جوزوا هذه الإجارة أي على تعليم القرآن حتى حكى
The importance of referring to the original source: The author of 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' and 'al-Jawhara Sharh al-Quduri' said: 'The fatwa is the validity of hiring', but the matter reversed on him, for the fatwa is the validity of hiring for teaching the Quran, not for its recitation. Then most of the later authors who came after him followed him in that and transmitted it, and it is a clear error. Rather, many of them said: 'The fatwa is on the validity of hiring for acts of worship.' They utter the expression absolutely, and say it is the madhhab of the later scholars, and some derive from that the validity of hiring for Hajj. All this is an error more blatant than the first error. For the transmissions from our three imams Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad have agreed: that hiring for acts of worship is invalid. But there came after them from among the mujtahids who are the people of takhrij and tarjih, so they gave fatwa on its validity for teaching the Quran. And from that also is what Qadikhan and others said: 'Trusts become guaranteed upon death due to ignorance except in three [cases].' Then the author of 'al-Bahr' followed up their statement and found seven others in addition to the three, and said: 'The origin of this expression is from al-Natafi, he erred in it, then they transmitted it.' And his statement: 'al-mujarrada' meaning that which is not within teaching or imamate. (1) His statement: 'Then most of the authors among them al-Qahistani, Mulla Miskin, and the author of al-Bahr, and some commentators of al-Ashbah, and al-Ala'i, and Ibn Abidin said: rather, the generality of the people of the era are upon that. (2) His statement: 'And they utter the expression' like Allamah Zayn ibn Nujaym and Shaykh Ala al-Din al-Haskafi, where they state in some of their statements that the fatwa is on the permissibility of hiring for acts of worship according to the later scholars, and that it is not absolute. Rather, al-Ramli rejected it in his Hashiya of al-Bahr in the book of Waqf, where he said: 'The fatwa is on the permissibility of taking compensation by istihsan for teaching the Quran, not for bare recitation,' as clarified in al-Tatarkhaniyya where he said: 'There is no meaning for the reward of the reciter for his recitation, because it is like wages, and hiring for that is invalid, and it is an innovation that none of the Caliphs did.' (3) His statement: 'And some derive' as said in al-Ashbah: 'Hiring of the pilgrim from the non-mahram is valid and he gets the like of his wage.' Then he attributed it to al-Khaniyya, and al-Shurunbulali rejected it in some of his treatises. That hiring for acts of worship is invalid, but there came after them from among the mujtahids who are the people of takhrij and tarjih, so they gave fatwa on its validity for teaching the Quran. (1) His statement: 'hiring for acts of worship is invalid' said in Khulasat al-Fatawa quoting from al-Asl: 'It is not permissible to hire for acts of worship such as teaching Quran, fiqh, adhan, reminding, Hajj, and warfare, meaning the wage is not obligatory. And according to the people of Madina it is permissible, and al-Shafi'i, Nasir, Isam, Abu Nasr al-Faqih, and Abu al-Layth took that. May Allah have mercy on them.' And the principle on which the prohibition of these things is based: that every act of worship specific to the Muslim is not permissible to hire for, because these things are acts of worship and religious deeds that are performed for the doer. Allah said: 'And that man has nothing except what he strives for.' So it is not permissible to take wages for them, like fasting and prayer. They argued for that with hadith, among them: what Ahmad narrated in his Musnad from Abd al-Rahman ibn Shibl: I heard the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, say: 'Recite the Quran and do not eat from it, and do not be harsh with it, and do not exaggerate in it, and do not seek to multiply [wealth] through it.' Among them: what al-Bazzaz narrated in his Musnad from Abd al-Rahman ibn Awf marfu'an similar to it. Among them: what al-Bayhaqi narrated in Shu'ab al-Iman from the hadith of Sulayman ibn Burayda from his father who said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever recites the Quran and eats from it with people, he will come on the Day of Resurrection with his face bone with no flesh on it.' (2) His statement: 'so they gave fatwa on its validity' said al-Marghinani and some of our scholars: 'They deemed valid by istihsan hiring for teaching the Quran today, due to the appearance of laziness in religious matters, because in refraining there is loss of Quran memorization, and upon it is the fatwa.' And in the text of al-Kanz after mentioning non-permissibility in what preceded: 'And the fatwa today is on the permissibility of hiring for teaching the Quran.' And likewise in other reliable books of the madhhab. And in al-Khulasa: 'There is no harm in taking wages for teaching the Quran in our time.' Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth said: I used to give fatwa in three matters, but I withdrew from them: I gave fatwa that it is not permissible to take wages for teaching the Quran, that it is not proper for a scholar to enter upon the ruler, and that he should not go to the countryside; I withdrew from all of them to avoid loss of Quran, due to the need of people and the ignorance of the people of the countryside. And Qadikhan said: 'The scholars of Balkh permitted this hiring, i.e., for teaching the Quran, until he narrated...'
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage is a methodological lesson for the mufti: the importance of verifying every transmitted statement against its original source (makhadhal asli). The author presents two examples of errors that arose because later scholars relied on secondary texts without checking the primary sources.

First example: The author of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Jawhara Sharh al-Quduri mistakenly stated that the fatwa was on the validity of hiring (ijarah) in general, when in fact the fatwa was specifically on hiring for teaching the Quran, not for mere recitation. Many later authors followed him blindly, and some even expanded it to hiring for all acts of worship and even for Hajj. This is a clear error because the three main Hanafi imams—Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—unanimously held that hiring for acts of worship is invalid. The original source (al-Asl) and the hadiths from the Prophet (peace be upon him) prohibit taking wages for reciting the Quran. However, later mujtahids (such as al-Marghinani and others) gave a fatwa allowing hiring for teaching the Quran due to necessity: people had become lazy, and forbidding it would lead to the neglect of Quran memorization. This ruling is an istihsan based on changed circumstances, but it does not overturn the original principle for other acts of worship. The error occurred because later scholars quoted the fatwa about teaching without the context and condition.

Second example: Qadikhan and others transmitted that 'amanat (trusts) become guaranteed (dhaman) upon death due to ignorance except in three cases.' The author of al-Bahr traced this statement and found that the original source (al-Natafi) had made an error, and the correct number of exceptions is ten (three plus seven more). This again shows the danger of not going back to the original source.

The commentary here serves to warn the mufti: never simply quote a later text without verifying its foundation. A ruling may be specific to a particular circumstance (like teaching Quran vs. recitation) or may have been misquoted. The mufti must be a researcher (muhaqqiq), not a mere transmitter.

Key Terms
المأخذ الأصلى (al-makhadhal al-asli): The original source text (like al-Asl, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.) from which a ruling is derived, as opposed to later secondary works.
الاستئجار على الطاعات (al-isti'jar 'ala al-ta'at): Hiring someone to perform an act of worship (e.g., reading Quran, teaching, Hajj) for payment.
تلاوة (tilawah): The mere recitation of Quran without teaching or instructing.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary reason the author of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj erred in his fatwa about ijarah?
A) He did not know the hadiths about hiring.
B) He confused the ruling for teaching Quran with the ruling for recitation.
C) He followed the opinion of Imam Shafi'i.
D) He relied on a weak transmission from Qadikhan.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must always trace a transmitted fatwa back to its original source (al-makhadhal al-asli) to avoid misapplying exceptions.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
10 min
Necessity in Hanafi Fatwa: Ijarah on Acts of Worship
Explaining the later Hanafi fatwa on hiring for ibadat due to necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'al-ḍarūrah tuqaddaru bi qadrihā' to identify when hiring for acts of worship is permissible and when it is not.

Core Idea
Necessity permits what is normally prohibited, but only to the exact extent of that necessity—and no further.

In classical Hanafi fiqh, hiring (ijarah) for acts of worship (ibadat) is invalid because worship requires sincerity (ikhlas) and cannot be a matter of wage. However, later scholars faced a crisis: teachers of Quran lost their stipends, threatening the very preservation of religious knowledge. They therefore developed a narrow exception based on necessity (ḍarūrah), governed by the maxim 'al-ḍarūrah tuqaddaru bi qadrihā'. This lesson examines that critical refinement and its correct application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the original ruling
State the original Hanafi position: ijarah on any act of worship is invalid (batil) because worship is for Allah alone and compensation negates sincerity.
The original ruling applies to teaching Quran, adhan, imamah, and all other forms of worship.
2
Recognize the necessity (ḍarūrah)
Identify the specific situation that triggered the exception: teachers' grants from the treasury were cut off, causing a real threat that Quranic education would cease entirely, leading to 'loss of religion' (ḍiyā‘ al-dīn).
Necessity here is not hypothetical; it must be actual and imminent.
3
Apply the qawida 'al-ḍarūrah tuqaddaru bi qadrihā'
The exception is only as wide as the necessity. The later scholars permitted ijarah specifically for teaching Quran, then analogized to adhan and imamah because they are public symbols of Islam. They did not permit it for mere recitation (tilawah) or other acts without a similar threat.
This step requires verifying that the necessity exists and that the ruling does not exceed it.
4
Distinguish permissible from impermissible cases
List the cases where ijarah is allowed: teaching Quran, adhan, imamah—only when necessary. List where it remains prohibited: recitation for deceased, dhikr, and other acts of worship not essential for the preservation of religion. If there is no necessity, the original ruling stands.
The author emphatically rejects the claim that the later madhhab allows hiring for mere recitation.
5
Draft fatwa with conditions
When issuing a fatwa, always state the necessity condition. Mufti must check: is there a real danger of religious loss? If yes, permit narrowly; if not, prohibit.
The mufti should also warn about the dangers of commercialization and loss of sincerity.

The importance of reviewing the original source. (Y) For necessity; for teachers used to receive grants from the treasury, but they were cut off. If hiring and taking wages were not valid, the Quran would be lost, and in that is the loss of religion, because teachers need to earn a living. And those after them also gave fatwa of its validity for the adhan and imamah, because they are among the symbols of religion, so they validated hiring for them due to necessity as well. This is what the later scholars after Abu Hanifa and his companions gave fatwa on, because they knew that if Abu Hanifa and his companions were in their era, they would have said the same and would have retracted their earlier statement. The texts, commentaries, and fatwa collections have unanimously transmitted the invalidity of hiring for acts of worship except what was mentioned, and they explained that with necessity, which is fear of loss of religion, and they explicitly stated that reasoning. So how can it be correct to say: 'The madhhab of the later scholars is the validity of hiring for mere recitation' without the aforementioned necessity? For if time passed and no one hired anyone for that, no harm would occur. Rather, harm occurred in hiring for it, where the Quran became a means of earning and a trade by which one does business, and the reciter among them does not recite anything purely for the sake of Allah, but only recites for the wage, and that is pure show (riya), which is intending the action for other than Allah. Then from where does he get the reward that the hirer intended to gift to his deceased? Imam Qadikhan said: 'Taking wages in exchange for dhikr prevents entitlement to reward.' And similar is in Fath al-Qadir regarding the mu'adhdhin taking wages. If one knew that there is no reward, he would not pay a single penny. So they devised means to collect forbidden wealth through dhikr and Quran, and people came to believe that is among the greatest acts of worship, while it is among the greatest abominations resulting from the opinion permitting hiring, along with other consequences such as consuming the wealth of orphans and sitting in their homes...
Source pages p. 56

Commentary
This passage discusses a key principle in Hanafi fatwa methodology: the role of necessity (darurah) in deriving rulings that differ from the original madhhab. The original position (from Abu Hanifa and his early companions) is that hiring (ijarah) for acts of worship (ta'at) is invalid, because worship requires sincerity (ikhlas) and cannot be contracted for wages. However, later Hanafi scholars faced a situation where teachers of Quran had lost their state stipends, and if hiring were not permitted, the teaching of Quran would cease, leading to the loss of religion. Therefore, they issued a fatwa allowing hiring for teaching Quran, and by extension for adhan and imamah, due to necessity. The text emphasizes that this is a narrow exception: the later scholars did not change the madhhab wholesale; they only permitted it where necessity existed. The author strongly refutes the notion that the later madhhab permits hiring for mere recitation (tilawah mujarradah) without such necessity. He argues that if there is no danger of the Quran being forgotten, then permitting hiring for recitation causes harm: it turns the Quran into a trade, leads to riya' (showing off), and destroys the reward intended by the hirer. He quotes Imam Qadikhan and Fath al-Qadir to show that taking wages for dhikr prevents reward. Thus, the fatwa is strictly limited to cases of necessity, and the mufti must always verify the presence of necessity before applying this exception.

Key Terms
الاستئجار على الطاعات (al-isti’jār ‘alā al-ṭā‘āt): Contracting a hire (ijarah) for performing acts of worship such as teaching Quran, adhan, imamah, and recitation
الضرورة (al-ḍarūrah): A situation that threatens the loss of religion (ḍiyā‘ al-dīn) if the original ruling is adhered to

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the condition that allows later Hanafi scholars to issue a fatwa permitting ijarah on acts of worship?
A) The act of worship is recommended
B) There is a necessity that prevents loss of religion
C) The hirer is wealthy
D) The wage is given as a gift

Key Takeaway
Later Hanafi scholars permit hiring for acts of worship only when necessity (ḍarūrah) threatens the loss of religion, and not beyond.

Repentance of the Prophet's Insulter Not Accepted
Ruling on non-acceptance of the sabb's repentance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the repentance of the sabb (Prophet's insulter) and apply the exception in the fatwa hierarchy.

Core Idea
Insulting the Prophet carries a lethal ruling that repentance cannot undo — an exception to general apostasy law.

As a mufti, you will encounter cases where general principles seem to apply, but a specific exception exists. This lesson examines one such critical exception: the one who insults the Prophet (saw). While an apostate's repentance is normally accepted and punishment waived, the Hanafi school based on strong precedent holds that the sabb's repentance does not avert execution. Understanding this ruling is essential for issuing correct fatwas on capital matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the rule and its scope
What exactly is the ruling? Who does it apply to? The sabb is anyone who insults or curses the Prophet (saw). The rule: he must be killed, and his repentance does not drop the killing.
The ruling is specific to the sabb, not all apostates.
2
Trace the evidence chain
The passage cites al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya, which refers to al-Shifa' (Maliki) and al-Sarim al-Maslul (Hanbali). Then Ibn al-Humam's reasoning: hating the Prophet makes one an apostate; insulting is worse, so the rule of apostasy is overridden.
The argument is qiyas awla (a fortiori).
3
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
If repentance were accepted, the sabb would be spared. Since it is not, execution is mandatory even after repentance. This is the practical consequence.
This distinguishes the sabb from the ordinary apostate.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that repentance is not accepted. This is affirmed by later scholars like Ibn al-Humam and is the view given fatwa precedence.
Muftis must follow this ruling in their fatwas.

Commentary
This passage discusses a specific rule in Hanafi fiqh: the one who insults the Prophet (saw) must be killed, and his repentance is not accepted to avert execution. The author cites al-Fatawa al-Bazzaziyya, which attributes this consensus to earlier sources: al-Shifa' (Maliki) and al-Sarim al-Maslul (Hanbali). Later scholars, including Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir, affirmed this ruling, reasoning that abusing the Prophet is worse than apostasy, and since the apostate's repentance would normally be accepted, here it is not. The passage ends with a quote from Shaykh al-Islam Amin al-Din ibn al-'Al, cut off. The lesson shows that not all rules of apostasy apply equally; insulting the Prophet has a special severity. The mufti must be aware of this exception when issuing fatwas on ridda.

Key Terms
الساب (al-sabb): One who insults or curses the Prophet Muhammad (saw)
التوبة (al-tawba): Repentance from sin, which normally removes punishment in apostasy cases
الردة (al-ridda): Apostasy from Islam

Key Takeaway
The sabb (Prophet's insulter) is executed even after repentance, an exception to general apostasy law.

The Hanafi Ruling on Reviling the Prophet: Repentance Accepted
Ruling-based discussion with source correction in mufti methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct Hanafi position on accepting the repentance of one who reviles the Prophet, and apply the rule of consulting original sources (al-ma'khadh al-asli) in mufti methodology.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school accepts the repentance of a reviler of the Prophet — he is killed only if he does not repent.

This passage addresses a common misconception that the Hanafi school does not accept the repentance of someone who reviles the Prophet Muhammad (s). The author, a Hanafi scholar, demonstrates that this view is incorrect by citing early authoritative sources of the madhhab. The lesson reinforces the crucial mufti methodology of referring to original works rather than later secondary compilations that may contain errors.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Misconception
Note the claim found in later works like al-Durar wa al-Ghurar that Hanafis do not accept repentance for reviling the Prophet. Recognize this as incorrect.
This is a common error in later texts.
2
Examine the Original Sources
Review the citations from Kitab al-Kharaj of Abu Yusuf, Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, and al-Nutaf. Each clearly states that the reviler is a murtadd and that his repentance is accepted.
These are early, authoritative texts of the Hanafi madhhab.
3
Understand the Author's Correction Method
See how the author uses these early texts to refute the mistaken attribution, emphasizing the need to consult al-ma'khadh al-asli (original sources).
This is a key method in rasm al-mufti.
4
Determine the Thamarah al-Khilaf
The practical difference is whether a person who reviles the Prophet and then repents is executed or spared. According to the Hanafi position, he is spared.
This affects fatwa in real cases.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-based discussion (rasm rule) from the field of mufti methodology. The author, a Hanafi scholar, corrects a common error found in later secondary works like al-Durar wa al-Ghurar, which attributed to the Hanafi school the view that one who reviles the Prophet is killed without accepting his repentance. The author demonstrates by citing original Hanafi sources (Kitab al-Kharaj of Abu Yusuf, Sharh Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, al-Nutaf) that the correct Hanafi position is that such a person is an apostate whose repentance is accepted, and he is only killed if he does not repent. The passage includes extensive footnotes confirming this from earlier authorities and showing that even non-Hanafi scholars like Ibn Taymiyya acknowledged the Hanafi view of accepting repentance. The author emphasizes the importance of referring to the original sources (al-ma'khadh al-asli) rather than relying on later compilations that may contain errors.

Key Terms
شاتم خير الأنام (shatim khayr al-anam): One who reviles the Prophet Muhammad (s) using insulting language.
قبول التوبة (qabul al-tawbah): Accepting the repentance of an apostate, which nullifies the death penalty.
مرتد (murtadd): A Muslim who abandons Islam, including through reviling the Prophet.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) He is killed without accepting his repentance.
B) His repentance is accepted, and he is not killed.
C) He is fined and imprisoned.
D) His repentance is accepted only if he was intoxicated.

Key Takeaway
The correct Hanafi position is to accept the repentance of one who reviles the Prophet, based on early authoritative sources; later attributions to the contrary are mistaken.

Guarantee of Pawn When Pledgee Claims Loss
Refutes the incorrect attribution that the pledgee guarantees full value without proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct Hanafi ruling on pledgee liability when the pawn is claimed lost, and evaluate the error in later Hanafi works that misattribute the Maliki position.

Core Idea
The pledgee guarantees the lesser of the pawn's value or the debt — proof or no proof.

In this passage, the author of Sharh 'Uqud Rasm al-Mufti corrects a common error found in later Hanafi texts. Some later works state that a pledgee who claims the pawn is lost must pay the full value unless he proves the loss. The author shows this is actually the Maliki position and restates the correct Hanafi ruling from earlier authoritative sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claimed ruling
What do al-Durar, Sharh al-Majma', and al-Tanwir state about the pledgee's liability when he claims the pawn is lost?
Look for the phrase 'yadmanu bida'wa al-halak bila burhan'.
2
Identify the Hanafi correction
How does the author respond to this claim? What does he attribute it to?
The author says this is actually the Maliki school.
3
Locate the authentic Hanafi position
What does al-Nutaf and earlier authorities say? What is the correct ruling?
'Our school is that he guarantees with the lesser of its value and the debt.'
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
What practical difference does this make in a fatwa?
Compare: full value vs. lesser of value or debt.

4. And from that is the issue of the guarantee of the pawn by the claim of destruction. It is mentioned in al-Durar (1) and Sharh al-Majma' of Ibn Malik that he (the pledgee) guarantees it by the claim of destruction without proof. And they are followed in the matn of al-Tanwir (2). And its consequence is that he guarantees its full value however much it is - and according to this the scholar Shaykh Khayr al-Din gave fatwa (3) and that he does not guarantee anything if he provides proof, whereas this is the school of Imam Malik, and our school is that he guarantees with the lesser of its value and the debt, with no difference between proving destruction with proof or without, as clarified in al-Nutaf... (followed by lexical note on النتف and footnotes).
Source pages p. 60

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling (rasm rule) concerning a common error in later Hanafi works. The author points out that al-Durar, Sharh al-Majma', and al-Tanwir state that if a pledgee (mortgagee) claims the pawned item has perished, he is liable for its full value without needing proof, and if he provides proof he is not liable. This, the author notes, is actually the Maliki position. The correct Hanafi position, as clarified in earlier works like al-Nutaf, is that the pledgee is liable only for the lesser amount between the value of the pawn and the debt, regardless of whether he can prove the loss. The author emphasizes that a mufti must refer to original Hanafi sources (like al-Nutaf) rather than relying on later compilations that may have adopted views of other schools.

Key Terms
رهن (rahn): A pawn or collateral given to secure a debt.
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee to compensate for loss or damage.
هلاك (halak): Destruction or loss of the pawned item.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as confirmed by the original sources in this passage, what amount must a pledgee (mortgagee) pay if he claims the pawned item has perished?
A) The full market value of the pawn without any reduction.
B) The lesser amount between the pawn's value and the debt.
C) Nothing, as long as he provides proof of destruction.
D) The full value only if he cannot provide witnesses.

Key Takeaway
The pledgee's liability for a lost pawn is capped at the lesser of the pawn's value or the debt, regardless of proof.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Source of Errors in Transmission and Duty of the Mufti
Ruling on the mufti's duty to verify sources

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main causes of error in fiqh transmissions and apply the principle that a mufti must verify rulings against earlier authoritative sources before issuing a fatwa.

Core Idea
A mufti must not rely on later books alone; errors arise from mis-copying or haste, and verification against original sources ensures correctness.

Errors in fiqh works are not random; they have identifiable causes. Ibn 'Abidin draws attention to two specific sources of error that can mislead a mufti. Understanding these causes and the duty to verify transmissions is essential for anyone who aspires to give sound fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Causes of Error
Read the Arabic phrase 'منشأها الخطأ في النقل، أو سبق النظر'. Understand that these are the two distinct origins of mistakes: error in copying from earlier works and haste in reading without careful reflection.
Note that 'سبق النظر' means the eye runs ahead of the mind, assuming correctness.
2
Trace the Author's Verification Method
Ibn 'Abidin describes his own method: he goes back to the earlier book (the 'asl') from which the later authors quoted, and he also collects the texts of other books that agree with the correct original. This is the gold standard for verification.
His hashiah Radd al-Muhtar is unparalleled because of this rigorous cross-checking.
3
Recognize the Danger for the Mufti of Little Knowledge
The author warns that a mufti with limited learning sees a ruling in one or more later books and assumes it is the madhhab. He fails to realize that while later books usually reflect the relied-upon view, they can contain errors.
This is a key rasm al-mufti principle: later fame is not a guarantee of correctness.
4
Apply the Principle to Your Own Study
Whenever you prepare a fatwa, do not stop at a famous later text like al-Durr al-Mukhtar or al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. Trace the ruling back to Zahir al-Riwayah texts (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.) to confirm it is the mufta bihi position.
This step saves you from issuing fatwa on an anomalous or erroneous view.

Source Text

شرح عقود رسم المفتی

منشأ السهو في النقل
الشرنبلالية عن عن "الحقائق"، ونبهت عليه في حاشيتي "رد المحتار على الدر المختار"، مع بيان من أفتى بما هو المذهب (۳)، ومن ردّ خلافه (۳). ولهذا الذي ذكرناه نظائر كثيرة، اتفق فيها صاحب البحر، و النهر، و "المنح"، و "الدر المختار" وغيرهم، وهي سهو، منشأها الخطأ في النقل، أو سبق النظر . نبهت عليها في حاشيتی رد المحتار لالتزامي فيها مراجعة الكتب المتقدمة التي يعزون المسألة إليها . فأذكر أصل العبارة التي وقع السهو في النقل عنها، وأضم إليها نصوص الكتب الموافقة لها، فلذا كانت تلك الحاشية عديمة النظير فى بابها ، لا يستغنى أحد عن تطلابها، أسأله سبحانه أن يعينني على إتمامها (٢).
فإذا نظر قليل الاطلاع، ورأى المسألة مسطورة في كتاب أو أكثر، يظن أن هذا هو المذهب، ويفتى به، ويقول : إن هذه الكتب للمتأخرين الذين اطلعوا على كتب من قبلهم وحرروا فيها ما عليه العمل، ولم يدر أن ذلك أغلبى، وأنه يقع منهم خلافه (۳)، كما سطرناه لك .

(۱) قوله : "عديمة النظير في بابها " في الفقه الحنفى، وشرح المهذب للإمام النووي في الفقه الشافعي مثله في دقة التصحيح، يقول الإمام في مقدمته : " قلت : لا يجوز لمفت على مذهب الشافعي إذا اعتمد النقل، أن يكتفي بمصنف ومصنفين ونحوهما من كتب المتقدمين وأكثر المتأخرين ؛ لكثرة الاختلاف بينهم في الجزم والترجيح؛ لأن هذا المفتى المذكور إنما ينقل مذهب الشافعي، ولا يحصل له وثوق بأن ما في المصنفين المذكورين ونحوهما هو مذهب الشافعى، أو الراجح منه ؛ لما فيها من الاختلاف. وهذا مما لا يتشكك فيه من له أدنى أنس بالمذهب، بل قد يجزم نحو عشرة من المصنفين بشيء وهو شاذ بالنسبة إلى الراجح في المذهب، ومخالف لما عليه الجمهور، وربما خالف نص الشافعي، أو نصوصا له. وسترى في هذا الشرح إن شاء الله تعالى أمثلة ذلك . وأرجو إن تم هذا الكتاب أنه يستغنى به عن كل مصنف، ويعلم به مذهب الشافعى علماً قطعياً إن شاء الله تعالى " ..

لا تحسب الفقه تمراً أنت أكله لن تبلغ الفقه حتى تلعق الصبرا
Explanation of the Contract of the Mufti, (1).. Page 61. Source of error in transmission. Sharunbulaliyya from 'al-Haqa'iq', and I alerted to it in my hashiah 'Radd al-Muhtar 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar', with a statement of who gave fatwa according to the madhhab (3), and who rejected its contrary (3). There are many parallels to what we have mentioned, agreed upon by the author of al-Bahr, al-Nahr, al-Minh, al-Durr al-Mukhtar and others, and they are errors, whose origin is mistake in transmission, or haste of sight. I alerted to them in my hashiah Radd al-Muhtar because I committed in it to reviewing the earlier books to which they attribute the issue. So I mention the original expression from which the error in transmission occurred, and I join to it the texts of the books that agree with it. Therefore that hashiah was unparalleled in its field; no one is independent of seeking it. I ask Him Almighty to help me complete it (2). Then when a person of little knowledge looks, and sees the issue written in one book or more, he thinks that this is the madhhab, and gives fatwa by it, and says: 'These books are from the later scholars who have consulted the books of those before them and have written in them what is acted upon.' And he did not know that this is only in most cases, and that contrary occurs from them (3), as we have written for you.
(1) His words: 'unparalleled in its field' – in Hanafi fiqh, and Sharh al-Muhadhdhab by Imam al-Nawawi in Shafi'i fiqh is similar in precision of correction. The Imam says in his introduction: 'I say: It is not permissible for a mufti on the Shafi'i madhhab, if he relies on transmission, to be satisfied with one or two works and the like from the books of the early scholars and most of the later ones, because of the abundance of disagreement among them in certainty and tarjih; because this mufti is only transmitting the Shafi'i madhhab, and he does not gain confidence that what is in those works is the Shafi'i madhhab or the preponderant view from it, due to the disagreement in them. This is not doubted by anyone with the slightest familiarity with the madhhab; rather, perhaps ten authors may affirm something that is anomalous relative to the preponderant view in the madhhab, and contrary to the position of the majority, and perhaps it contradicts the text of al-Shafi'i, or texts of his. And you will see in this commentary, Allah willing, examples of that. And I hope that if this book is completed, it will render all other works unnecessary, and the Shafi'i madhhab will be known with certainty, Allah willing.' (2) His words: 'to help me complete it' – I said: May Allah give him success in completion and assist him by His grace. He, may Allah have mercy on him, first began dictation from beginning to end, then started fair copying, beginning first from al-Ijarah to the end, then from the beginning of the book to the chapter of al-Qada, and when he reached its middle, he longed to witness the Lord of lords... (Mazhari) So his blessed son al-Sayyid Muhammad Ala' al-Din hastened to extract the marginal notes from his father's copy. (3) His words: 'and that contrary occurs from them' – the commentator said in his treatise 'Tanbih al-Wulah wa al-Hukkam': If you say: if the matter is so, it is not proper for the mufti to give fatwa merely by consulting a book, even if that book is famous. I say: Yes, it is so. Poetry: "Do not think fiqh is like dates you eat; you will not attain fiqh until you taste patience."
Source pages p. 61

Commentary
This passage is a methodological ruling concerning the duty of a mufti to verify transmitted rulings from original sources. The author, Ibn 'Abidin, begins by discussing the source of errors (سهو) in fiqh works. He points out that many mistakes arise from errors in transmission (خطأ في النقل) or from haste (سبق النظر). He states that he has noted such errors in his gloss 'Radd al-Muhtar' and has committed to reviewing the earlier books to which rulings are attributed. He mentions that there are many parallels in the works of later scholars like al-Bahr, al-Nahr, etc., and these are errors.

He then warns against the mufti of little knowledge who sees a ruling in one or more later books and assumes that it is the madhhab, not realizing that while most of the time later books reflect the relied-upon position, sometimes they contain errors contrary to the madhhab. This is a crucial rasm al-mufti principle: a mufti must not give fatwa based solely on later works without verifying against earlier authoritative sources, because even a famous book may contain an anomalous ruling.

The marginal note (1) provides a comparative example from Imam al-Nawawi's introduction to Sharh al-Muhadhdhab, where he emphasizes that a Shafi'i mufti cannot rely on just one or two later works due to disagreements; the same principle applies in the Hanafi school. Note (2) provides biographical details about the author's writing process. Note (3) quotes a poem reminding that attaining fiqh requires patience and rigorous verification.

Thus the core lesson: a mufti must trace rulings back to the original sources (Zahir al-Riwayah) and not accept later transmissions uncritically. This falls under the rasm al-mufti and mufti adab categories.

Key Terms
منشأ السهو في النقل (Mansha' al-sahw fi al-naql): The origin of errors in transmitting legal rulings from earlier authorities to later works.
سبق النظر (Sabq al-nazar): Haste of sight; a cause of error where one sees something in a book and assumes it is correct without careful reflection.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Ibn 'Abidin, what are the two main sources of error (سهو) in fiqh transmissions?
A) Forgetfulness and ignorance
B) Error in transmission and haste of sight
C) Intentional distortion and weak memory
D) Biased reporting and lack of knowledge

Key Takeaway
A mufti must verify any ruling by tracing it back to the original Zahir al-Riwayah sources; later books alone, even if multiple and famous, are not sufficient and may contain errors.

The Prohibition of Issuing Fatwa by Mere Book Reading
Ruling forbidding fatwa without proper training and its conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three conditions required for a mufti and apply the rule that one who issues fatwa without these conditions is subject to ta'zir.

Core Idea
A mufti must have complete proficiency, teacher certification, and a mental faculty; mere book reading is insufficient.

This lesson explains a foundational rule of Hanafi usul al-ifta: that issuing fatwas requires more than mere book knowledge. Using a vivid example of a mistaken fatwa, the author establishes the conditions for a qualified mufti and warns of severe consequences for those who violate this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Extract the core prohibition: it is not permissible for one who reads books alone without a teacher to issue fatwas.
2
Extract the conditions for a mufti
List the three conditions mentioned in the commentary: complete proficiency, training under experts, and a mental faculty (malakah nafsaniyyah).
These are from the expanded explanation after the quote from Ibn Hajar.
3
Understand the evidence
Analyze the quotation from Ibn Hajar al-Haytami and the reference to al-Nawawi; note the emphasis on teacher certification and the danger of relying on few books.
The evidence is a fatwa (dalil naqli).
4
Apply to a modern scenario
Consider a contemporary person who learns fiqh only through online resources without a qualified teacher; apply the rule that they cannot issue fatwas.
This connects the classical rule to current challenges.

(۲) قوله : بخلاف الماهر بيان لما يشترط للمفتى وهى على ما ذكره ثلاثة : -١- المهارة التامة في الفقه، وتحصل بالاشتغال في الفقه وتدريسه ومذاكرته ومطالعته، مدة معتدة بها . -٢- التفقه لدى الأساتذة المهرة والتمرين على الإفتاء عندهم، ثم لا يجوز له الإفتاء ولا القضاء إلا إذا شهد له مشايخه بأهليته وأذنوا له بهما . وهذا لأن الفقهاء كثيراً ما يذكرون المسألة مطلقا ويريدون بها الحكم المقيد بالقيود التي يجب أن يلاحظ هنا لكن يتركونها اعتماداً على ذكرها في مواضعها وعلى فهم السامع، فمجرد مطالعة كتب الفقه ربما يؤدى إلى خلاف المقصود . - - الحصول على ملكة نفسانية يتيسر بها معرفة وجوه الفقه وما يتعلق بها، ويسمى فقه النفس" ، و "جودة القريحة"، وذلك فضل الله يؤتيه من يشاء، فليجأ المتصدى للإفتاء إلى جناب ربه، حتى يفوز بمقصده . (۳) قوله : "إذا تسور" مأخوذ من قولهم: "فلان" تسور الحائط " إذا صعد عليه، أو من قولهم: "تسور السوار إذا لبسه، وعلى كل من الوجهين يكون الكلام مبنيا على التشبيه. (مظ)
63 Issuing fatwa by reading books by himself. Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti. And I had once given a fatwa on a matter of waqf in agreement with what is written in most books, and the matter was ambiguous for Shaykh Alaa al-Din al-Haskafi, the pillar of the later scholars, so he mentioned it in al-Durr al-Mukhtar contrary to correctness, and my answer that I gave fell into the hands of a group of muftis of the country, who wrote on its back contrary to what I had given, agreeing with what is in al-Durr al-Mukhtar, and some of these muftis added: 'This which is in al-Ala'i is what is acted upon because he is the pillar of the later scholars, and if you have anything contrary to it, we do not accept it from you.' So look at this great ignorance, and recklessness in Islamic rulings, and proceeding to give fatwa without knowledge and without review. Would that this speaker had consulted the gloss of the scholar Shaykh Ibrahim al-Halabi on al-Durr al-Mukhtar; for it (1) is closest to him, and he pointed out in it that al-Ala'i made a mistake in expression. Section: It is not permissible to give fatwa for one who reads books by himself and has not studied fiqh under an expert teacher, and the obligation to punish the one who violates this. And I have seen in the fatwas of the scholar Ibn Hajar that he was asked about a person who reads and studies the fiqh books by himself, and he did not have a teacher, and he gives fatwa and relies on his study in books, is it permissible for him or not? For if fiqh were acquired merely by the ability to review a matter from its sources, it would be the easiest thing, and there would be no need to study fiqh under an expert teacher and a penetrating brilliant intellect. Poetry: If this knowledge were attained by wishes, you would not see an ignorant person in the world. (Rasa'il Ibn Abidin 2/338) (1) His saying: 'for it' – the pronoun refers to 'the gloss', and his saying 'to it' means to this speaker. The meaning: that the gloss of the scholar al-Halabi was easily available to this speaker. 64 Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti Issuing fatwa by reading books by himself. So he answered with his saying: 'It is not permissible for him to give fatwa in any way, because he is a layman ignorant, not knowing what he says. Rather, one who takes knowledge from reliable teachers is not allowed to give fatwa from a book, nor from two books.' Rather, al-Nawawi (may Allah have mercy on him) said: 'Nor from ten, for ten and twenty may all rely on a weak statement in the madhhab, so it is not permissible to imitate them in it.' (1) Unlike the expert (2) who took knowledge from its people, and developed a mental faculty in it, for he distinguishes the correct from others, and knows the matters and what relates to them in the proper way. This is the one who gives fatwa to people and is fit to be a mediator between them and Allah Almighty. As for other than him, if he vaults (3) into this noble position, he is subject to severe punishment and strong deterrent that deters his likes from this ugly matter that leads to countless evils. And Allah knows best. End. (1) His saying: 'so it is not permissible to imitate them in it' – refer to the introduction of al-Majmu' Sharh al-Muhadhdhab attached to this book, chapter on the rulings of muftis, seventh issue. (2) His saying: 'unlike the expert' – an explanation of the conditions for the mufti, which according to what he mentioned are three: 1- Complete proficiency in fiqh, attained by engaging in fiqh, teaching it, discussing it, and studying it for a considerable period. 2- Studying fiqh under expert teachers and training in giving fatwa under them. Then it is not permissible for him to give fatwa or judge unless his teachers testify to his competence and permit him to do both. This is because jurists often mention a matter absolutely and intend by it the restricted ruling with the restrictions that must be observed here, but they omit them relying on their mention in other places and on the listener's understanding. So mere study of fiqh books may lead to contrary to the intent. 3- Acquiring a mental faculty through which ease in understanding the aspects of fiqh and what relates to it becomes available, called 'fiqh of the soul' and 'sharpness of talent.' That is a favor of Allah which He gives to whom He wills. So let the one who aspires to give fatwa turn to his Lord to achieve his goal. (3) His saying: 'if he vaults' – derived from their saying: 'So-and-so vaulted the wall' meaning he climbed over it, or from their saying: 'he put on the bracelet' meaning he wore it. In either case, the speech is built on comparison. (Mazhar)
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage from Sharh Uqud Rasm al-Mufti is a methodological rule (rasm al-mufti) concerning the prohibition of issuing fatwas based solely on reading books without proper training under a qualified teacher. The author begins with a personal anecdote to illustrate the danger: he once gave a fatwa on waqf consistent with most books, but the later scholar Allama al-Haskafi (author of al-Durr al-Mukhtar) inadvertently recorded a mistaken opposite view. Some later muftis, blindly following al-Haskafi's authority, rejected the correct view and insisted on the erroneous one, demonstrating arrogance and ignorance. The author then states the rule clearly: a person who has only read books without studying under a master (ustadh mahir) is not allowed to issue fatwas, and violators must be punished (ta'zir). He supports this by quoting a fatwa from Ibn Hajar al-Haytami, who explicitly forbids such a person from giving fatwa. The explanation includes a necessary condition: even if one has studied under teachers, one should not rely solely on a few books. Al-Nawawi is quoted that even ten or twenty scholars may follow a weak opinion, so one cannot blindly follow them. The passage then distinguishes the true expert (mahir) who has three qualities: (1) complete proficiency in fiqh attained through long study, teaching, and discussion; (2) learning under expert teachers and obtaining their permission to issue fatwas; and (3) developing a mental faculty (malakah nafsaniyyah) that grants intuitive understanding of fiqh. This faculty is called 'fiqh al-nafs' or 'joodat al-qarihah'. Finally, it emphasizes that anyone who usurps this role without these qualifications deserves severe punishment. The overall message is that fatwa is a serious responsibility requiring thorough training and spiritual development, not mere book knowledge.

Key Terms
المهارة التامة (al-mahārah al-tāmmah): Complete proficiency in fiqh attained by long-term engagement in teaching, discussion, and study of fiqh.
ملكة نفسانية (malakah nafsāniyyah): A mental faculty developed through deep study and divine grace that allows the mufti to correctly understand and apply fiqh.
تعزير (ta‘zīr): Discretionary punishment imposed by the ruler for offenses that do not have a fixed hadd penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling for a person who reads fiqh books on his own without a teacher and issues fatwas?
A) Permissible if he has good understanding.
B) Not permissible at all, and he should be punished.
C) Permissible only if he consults multiple books.
D) Permissible but discouraged.

Key Takeaway
Issuing fatwa requires complete proficiency, teacher certification, and a mental faculty; mere book reading is prohibited and incurs ta'zir.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Obligation to Give Fatwa by Zahir al-Riwayah
Rule that fatwa must follow Zahir al-Riwayah with exception for corrected narrations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the rasm al-mufti rule that fatwa must be based on Zahir al-Riwayah and identify when a corrected non-Zahir al-Riwayah opinion may be followed.

Core Idea
Fatwa follows the well-known transmitted rulings; exceptions require explicit correction by scholars.

This passage establishes a foundational rule in Hanafi ifta: the mufti is bound by the Zahir al-Riwayah – the authoritative transmissions from Imam Muhammad's six books. However, later scholars may correct a different narration, and then that corrected opinion is followed. For a muqallid judge, the restriction is even stricter: he cannot use weak or anomalous narrations unless scholars explicitly permit fatwa on them. This rule ensures consistency and prevents arbitrary selection of opinions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Main Rule
State the rule: 'It is obligatory to give fatwa based on Zahir al-Riwayah.' Recognize that this means the rulings from Muhammad al-Shaybani's six well-known books are the default source for fatwa.
This applies even if later scholars did not explicitly declare these rulings as correct.
2
Understand the Exception
If later scholars explicitly correct a narration from outside Zahir al-Riwayah, then that corrected opinion is followed. This is an exception to the general rule, as stated: 'If they corrected another narration… one follows what they corrected.'
The correction must be explicit.
3
Apply to Muqallid Judge
A muqallid judge may only judge by Zahir al-Riwayah and cannot use weak or anomalous narrations (riwāya shādhdha) unless the scholars explicitly state that fatwa is upon that narration. If he rules otherwise, his judgment is invalid.
The authorities cited include al-Tarsusi, Allamah Qasim, Ibn Nuwas, and the author of al-Bahr.
4
Analyze the Example
The example of the palm (kaff) being awra: Zahir al-Riwayah considers it awra, but some later scholars considered it not awra, deeming that more correct (though not Zahir al-Riwayah). This illustrates how the exception works in practice.
From Radd al-Muhtar 1:405.

Source Text

مطلب يجب الإفتاء بظاهر الرواية إلا إذا صرحوا بخلافه الإفتاء بظاهر الرواية وقولى: "أو كان ظاهر الرواية ... إلخ " معناه : أن ما كان من المسائل في الكتب التي رويت عن محمد بن الحسن رواية ظاهرة، يفتى به وإن لم يصرحوا بتصحيحه، نعم ! لو صححوا رواية أخرى من غير كتب ظاهر الرواية، يتبع ما صححوه (1) . قال العلامة الطرسوسي في أنفع الوسائل" في مسألة الكفالة إلى شهر : "إن القاضي المقلّد لا يجوز له أن يحكم (3) إلا بما هو ظاهر الرواية، لا بالرواية الشاذة، إلا أن ينصوا على أن الفتوى عليها " . اهـ . (1) قوله : " يتبع ما صححوه " مثاله ما في الدر المختار وحاشيته : " فظهر الكف عورة على المذهب". وقال في رد المحتار: أى ظاهر الرواية. وفي مختلفات قاضيخان وغيرها : أنه ليس بعورة، وأيده في شرح المنية بثلاثة أوجه . وقال : فكان هو الأصح وإن كان غير ظاهر الرواية . (رد المحتار : ٤٠٥/١) (2) قوله : " إن القاضي المقلّد لا يجوز له أن يحكم " قال العلامة قاسم في فتواه : وليس للقاضي المقلد أن يحكم بالضعيف؛ لأنه ليس من أهل الترجيح، فلا يعدل عن الصحيح إلا لقصد غير جميل . ولو حكم لا ينفذ ؛ لأن قضاءه قضاء بغير الحق ؛ لأن الحق هو الصحيح. وما وقع من أن القول الضعيف يتقوى بالقضاء، المراد به قضاء المجتهد، كما بين في موضعه . وقال ابن نواس : " وأما المقلد المحض : فلا يقضى إلا بما عليه الفتوى والعمل". وقال صاحب "البحر في بعض رسائله : "أما القاضي المقلّد فليس له الحكم إلا بالصحيح المفتى به فى مذهبه. ولا ينفذ قضاؤه بالقول الضعيف" . (مظ)
Topic: It is obligatory to give fatwa according to Zahir al-Riwayah unless they explicitly state otherwise. Giving fatwa according to Zahir al-Riwayah. And my saying: 'or it was Zahir al-Riwayah... etc.' means: what is among the issues in the books that were narrated from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan with a clear narration (riwāya ẓāhira) is given fatwa upon even if they did not explicitly declare it as correct. Yes, if they corrected another narration from outside the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, one follows what they corrected. (1) He said: 'one follows what they corrected' — an example is in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and its gloss: 'So it appeared that the palm is naked [ʿawra] according to the madhhab.' And in Radd al-Muhtar: i.e., Zahir al-Riwayah. In Mukhtalafat Qadikhan and others: that it is not ʿawra, and it was supported in Sharh al-Munya with three aspects, and he said: so it is the most correct even though it is not Zahir al-Riwayah. (Radd al-Muhtar 1:405) (2) He said: 'The muqallid judge is not permitted to judge' — Allamah Qasim said in his fatwa: The muqallid judge has no right to judge by the weak [opinion] because he is not one of those who can weigh evidences. So he should not deviate from the correct except for a bad motive. If he judges with it, it is not executed because his judgment is a judgment without truth, for the truth is the correct one. What has occurred that the weak opinion gains strength by judgment, that is meant by the judgment of a mujtahid, as explained in its place. Ibn Nuwas said: 'As for the pure muqallid, he should not judge except according to what the fatwa and practice are upon.' The author of al-Bahr said in some of his treatises: 'As for the muqallid judge, he does not have the right to judge except by the correct opinion that is given fatwa upon in his madhhab. And his judgment with the weak opinion is not executed.'
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage establishes a critical rasm rule in Hanafi ifta: a mufti must give fatwa based on Zahir al-Riwayah—the well-known and reliably transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's six books. The author explains that even if later scholars did not explicitly declare such a ruling correct, it is still the basis for fatwa. However, if they explicitly correct a different narration from outside Zahir al-Riwayah, that corrected opinion is followed. The text then applies this rule to the muqallid judge, citing al-Tarsusi: a muqallid judge may only judge by Zahir al-Riwayah, not by anomalous narrations (riwāya shādhdha), unless the scholars explicitly state that fatwa is upon that anomalous narration. The footnotes provide examples, including the issue of the palm as awra, where there is a difference between Zahir al-Riwayah (it is awra) and other reports (not awra), yet the latter was considered more correct by some later scholars. The rule ensures consistency and authority in Islamic legal practice.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zāhir al-Riwāya): The well-known transmitted rulings from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani's six books (Zahir al-Riwayah: al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Ziyadat).
رواية شاذة (Riwāya Shādhdha): An anomalous or isolated narration that is not widely transmitted in the madhhab, not to be used for fatwa unless explicitly endorsed.
قاضي مقلّد (Qāḍī Muqallid): A judge who follows the Hanafi madhhab but is not a mujtahid, thus bound by the rulings of the madhhab as transmitted in authoritative books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Ignore it and stick to Zahir al-Riwayah
B) Follow that corrected narration
C) Follow the opinion of the majority of scholars
D) Give the seeker a choice

Key Takeaway
The default for fatwa is Zahir al-Riwayah, but a corrected opinion from a later scholar takes precedence when explicitly declared as such.

Rasm al-Mufti — Rules of Issuing Fatwa
intermediate
8 min
Fatwa Must Follow Zahir al-Riwayah
Ruling on the basis of fatwa in the Hanafi school

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Zahir al-Riwayah as the primary source for fatwa in the Hanafi school and apply the rule that only manifest narrations are followed unless later scholars explicitly adopt an anomalous narration.

Core Idea
Fatwa in the Hanafi school is built upon the manifest narrations (Zahir al-Riwayah); anomalous narrations are not followed unless the later masters explicitly correct them.

This lesson tackles a foundational principle of Hanafi fatwa: which narrations are authoritative for issuing rulings. The passage defines the hierarchy between the manifest narrations (Zahir al-Riwayah) and anomalous narrations (riwayah shadhdhah), and clarifies that a muqallid judge is bound by this hierarchy. Understanding this rule prevents haphazard fatwa and ensures consistency.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary source category
Recognize that Zahir al-Riwayah refers to the well-known narrations transmitted from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani in his six core books. These are the default for fatwa.
Zahir al-Riwayah is the first tier in the Hanafi textual hierarchy.
2
Note the default rule
The passage states that fatwa is given by Zahir al-Riwayah even if later scholars did not explicitly declare it correct. It is inherently reliable.
This avoids the need for independent verification of each ruling.
3
Recognize the exception
If later scholars explicitly correct an anomalous narration (outside Zahir al-Riwayah), then that corrected view becomes the basis for fatwa. The correction must be explicit.
Example: the palm ‘awrah issue – the mufta bihi remains the Zahir al-Riwayah view until explicit correction.
4
Apply to the muqallid judge
A muqallid judge cannot weigh evidence; he must judge only by Zahir al-Riwayah. Judging by weak narrations renders his judgment void.
This protects the integrity of the judiciary.
5
Confirm the consequence
If a muqallid judge issues a ruling based on a weak narration, it is invalid and not enforceable.
The text cites multiple authorities on this point.

يجب الإفتاء بظاهر الرواية

الإفتاء بظاهر الرواية
وقولى: "أو كان ظاهر الرواية ... إلخ " معناه : أن ما كان من المسائل في الكتب التي رويت عن محمد بن الحسن رواية ظاهرة، يفتى به وإن لم يصرحوا بتصحيحه، نعم ! لو صححوا رواية أخرى من غير كتب ظاهر الرواية، يتبع ما صححوه (۱) .

(مظ)
Topic: It is obligatory to give fatwa according to the manifest narration, unless they explicitly state contrary to it. Giving fatwa by the manifest narration. And my statement: 'or it was the manifest narration ... etc.' means: whatever matters are in the books that were transmitted from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan as a manifest narration, fatwa is given by it even if they did not explicitly declare it as correct. Yes, if they corrected another narration from other than the books of manifest narration, that which they corrected is followed (1). Allamah Tarsusi said in 'Anfa' al-Wasa'il' concerning the issue of guaranty until a month: 'Indeed the muqallid judge is not permitted to judge except by what is the manifest narration, not by the anomalous narration, unless they specify that the fatwa is upon it.' End. (1) His statement: 'that which they corrected is followed.' An example is what is in al-Durr al-Mukhtar and its gloss: 'Thus it appears that the palm is not nakedness according to the madhhab.' And it was said in Radd al-Muhtar: i.e. the manifest narration. And in different rulings of Qadikhan and others: it is not nakedness, and it was supported in Sharh al-Munyah by three aspects. And he said: so it is the most sound even if it is not the manifest narration. (Radd al-Muhtar 1/405) (2) His statement: 'Indeed the muqallid judge is not permitted to judge' – Allamah Qasim said in his fatwa: It is not for the muqallid judge to judge by the weak (narration) because he is not from the people of tarjih (weighing), so he should not deviate from the sound except for an unseemly purpose. And if he judges, it is not executed, because his judgment is a judgment without right, because the right is the sound. And what has occurred that the weak statement is strengthened by judgment, the intent is the judgment of a mujtahid, as explained in its place. And Ibn Nuwas said: 'As for the pure muqallid, he does not judge except by what the fatwa and practice are upon.' And the author of al-Bahr said in some of his epistles: 'As for the muqallid judge, he has no judgment except by the sound and mufta bihi (relied upon for fatwa) in his madhhab. And his judgment by the weak statement is not executed.'
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the methodology of issuing fatwa (rasm al-mufti). It establishes that the primary source for fatwa is the Zahir al-Riwayah – the manifest narrations transmitted from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The author clarifies that even if later scholars have not explicitly declared a ruling from these books as 'sahih' (correct), it is still valid for fatwa. However, if they explicitly correct a different narration from outside these books, that corrected view is followed. The quote from Allamah Tarsusi emphasizes that a muqallid judge (one who is not a mujtahid) must only judge by the manifest narration, not by anomalous narrations, unless the scholars explicitly state that the fatwa is on the anomalous one. The footnotes provide examples: In the issue of whether the palm is 'awrah (nakedness), the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that it is 'awrah, being the Zahir al-Riwayah, even though some later scholars supported the opposite with three proofs. But because that opposite is not Zahir al-Riwayah, it is not followed for fatwa unless later scholars explicitly adopt it. The second footnote discusses that a muqallid judge cannot base a judgment on weak narrations, and if he does, his judgment is void.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The manifest narrations transmitted from Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani through well-known chains; the primary source for fatwa in the Hanafi school.
رواية شاذة (riwayah shadhdhah): An anomalous narration that is not part of the Zahir al-Riwayah; not to be followed for fatwa unless later scholars explicitly adopt it.
القاضي المقلّد (al-qadi al-muqallid): A judge who is not a mujtahid and must follow the rulings of his madhhab [i.e., the Hanafi school] and cannot weigh evidence independently.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what should a muqallid judge base his judgment on?
A) Any narration found in Hanafi books
B) Only the manifest narration (Zahir al-Riwayah)
C) The most widely known narration even if not in Zahir al-Riwayah
D) His own reasoning and preference

Key Takeaway
Fatwa in the Hanafi school defaults to the manifest narrations (Zahir al-Riwayah); only explicit later correction can override them.

The Six Books of Zahir al-Riwayah: Definition and Dispute
Defining the books of Zahir al-Riwayah and their significance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah and state the relied-upon opinion regarding their composition.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah consists of six books by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, transmitted with high reliability.

The term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' is fundamental for fatwa in the Hanafi madhhab. This passage defines which books constitute this category and notes disagreements among later scholars. Understanding these sources ensures you derive rulings from the most authoritative texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the term being defined
The passage defines 'Zahir al-Riwayah' as a set of books compiled by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Recognize that this is a source hierarchy concept.
The term appears in the matn (verse).
2
List the six books as per the matn
The matn explicitly enumerates: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut.
These are sometimes called 'al-Usul' (the principles).
3
Compare with the dispute in the commentary
The commentary cites different opinions: some exclude al-Siyar al-Saghir, others exclude both al-Siyar books, and some include al-Muhit instead.
Disagreement stems from varying definitions of tawatur and shuhra.
4
Determine the mufta bihi position
The mashhur (well-known) position is the six books as in the matn. The other views are considered weak.
This hierarchy affects which sources are prioritized in fatwa.

(مظ)
(۲) قوله : 'حرر فيها ' التحرير : التهذيب والتنقيح، يقال: حرر الكتاب : إذا أخلاه عن الحشو والزوائد .
(۳) قوله : 'الجامع الصغير ' قد ألفت في المذهب تأليف سميت بـ الجامع فوق ما ينوف من أربعين . (مظ)
And the books of Zahir al-Riwayah are six, and they are also called the principles. Muhammad al-Shaybani compiled them, containing the Nu'mani madhhab. Al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir and al-Saghir. Then al-Ziyadat with al-Mabsut, transmitted with a guaranteed chain. Likewise, he has masa'il al-nawadir, whose chains in the books are not apparent. And after them are masa'il al-nawazil, extracted by the mashayikh with evidences. (1) His statement: 'And the books of Zahir al-Riwayah.' He said in Ta'aliq al-Anwar on al-Durr al-Mukhtar: Some did not count al-Siyar al-Saghir among them, and al-Tahawi mentioned in his glosses that some did not count al-Siyar in its two parts among them. And it is said in Nata'ij al-Afkar: The meaning of Zahir al-Riwayah according to the jurists is the transmission of al-Jami'an, al-Mabsut, and al-Ziyadat, and the meaning of non-Zahir al-Riwayah is other transmissions. Similarly in al-Inayah: The intended meaning of al-Usul is al-Jami'an, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut. In Miftah al-Sa'adah: They refer to al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, and al-Jami'an as the transmission of the principles. And they refer to al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir as Zahir al-Riwayah and famous transmission. Al-Sayyid al-Jurjani said in al-Istilahat: Zahir al-madhhab and Zahir al-riwayah both refer to what is in al-Mabsut, al-Jami'an, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. Some said: Zahir al-Riwayah is al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, and al-Muhit, but there is something in that. (Mazhir) (2) His statement: 'He compiled in them.' Al-tahrir: refinement and correction. It is said: He compiled the book: when he emptied it of extraneous additions. (3) His statement: 'Al-Jami' al-Saghir.' There have been compiled in the madhhab works named al-Jami' over forty. (Mazhir)

Commentary
This passage defines the term 'Zahir al-Riwayah' in the Hanafi madhhab. It begins with the matn (verse) enumerating six books compiled by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani: al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Ziyadat, and al-Mabsut. These are the foundational texts of the school. The commentary then discusses varying opinions on which books exactly constitute Zahir al-Riwayah. Some exclude al-Siyar al-Saghir; others exclude both al-Siyar books. Most authorities include the 'three books' (al-Jami'an and al-Ziyadat) as 'al-Usul', while others include al-Mabsut as well. The passage also clarifies the meaning of 'tahrir' (compilation) and notes the many works titled 'al-Jami'. The overall point is that Zahir al-Riwayah texts are those transmitted with high reliability, forming the basis for fatwa.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Ẓāhir al-Riwāyah): The apparent/well-known transmission; the six books of Imam Muhammad that are transmitted with tawatur or high reliability.
الجامع الصغير (al-Jāmiʿ al-Ṣaghīr): One of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah; a collection by Imam Muhammad.
المبسوط (al-Mabsūṭ): One of the six books; a detailed work by Imam Muhammad.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) al-Mabsut
C) al-Hidayah
D) al-Ziyadat

Key Takeaway
The six books of Zahir al-Riwayah are the most authoritative sources for Hanafi fatwa, transmitted with tawatur.

The Three Layers of Hanafi Masail
Classifying Hanafi legal issues into three hierarchical layers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three layers of Hanafi masail and classify a given ruling within the hierarchy to determine its authority for fatwa.

Core Idea
Zahir al-Riwayah is the binding layer; other layers require scrutiny against usul.

Not all Hanafi rulings carry the same weight. This passage establishes a three-layer hierarchy—Masail al-Usul (Zahir al-Riwayah), Nawadir, and Nawazil—that guides a mufti in deciding which ruling to rely upon. Understanding this hierarchy prevents the error of treating all transmitted opinions as equally authoritative.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three layers
Read the passage and list the three classes: Masail al-Usul (first layer), then implicitly the other two (Nawadir and Nawazil). Note that the passage elaborates mainly on the first.
The other two layers are mentioned in the footnote as 'rare transmissions' and 'later derivations'.
2
Understand the first layer (Masail al-Usul)
This layer is also called Zahir al-Riwayah. It comprises rulings transmitted directly from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani—the three founders. The transmission is by tawatur or shuhra, ensuring reliability.
The term 'ashabuna' primarily refers to these three imams.
3
Learn the alternative four-fold division
The footnote from Adab al-Ifta' splits the layers into four categories: established rulings (accepted always), rare transmissions (accepted only if consistent with usul), agreed-upon later derivations (accepted always), and disputed later derivations (examined against usul and parallels).
This alternative provides a more granular tool for evaluation.
4
Apply the hierarchy to determine fatwa authority
If a mas'ala belongs to Zahir al-Riwayah, the mufti may issue a fatwa directly without further verification. If it is from a lower layer, he must check its agreement with usul and, for disputed derivations, also consult parallels.
The first layer is the default authority.
5
Recognize the linguistic nuance of 'Zahir al-Riwayah'
The phrase is an idafa maqluba (inverted genitive) meaning 'the apparent transmission'—like 'kabir al-hajm' meaning 'hajm kabir'. This reflects that the transmission itself is apparent (clear and well-known).
Understanding this helps avoid misinterpreting the term as a mere label.

فالإضافة فيه مقلوب من التوصيف ككبير الحجم فإنه في معنى حجم كبير
The Classification of Masail
Section
The classification of masail is three.
Know that the masail of our companions (1) the Hanafis are of three classes (2):
First: Masail al-Usul, also called Zahir al-Riwayah (3). They are masail transmitted from the founders of the madhhab: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them. They are called 'the three scholars.' Zufar, al-Hasan, and others who took fiqh from Abu Hanifa may be joined to them, but the common and widespread is what is in Zahir al-Riwayah.
(1) His statement: 'our companions.' Ibn Abidin said: The famous usage of 'our companions' is for our three imams: Abu Hanifa and his two companions, as mentioned in Sharh al-Whabaniyyah. As for the mashayikh, in Waqf al-Nahr from Allama Qasim: The meaning in terminology is those who did not meet the Imam. (Radd al-Muhtar 4:495 - Mazhir)
(2) His statement: 'upon three classes.' It has also been divided in another way into four sections: A section established in the apparent madhhab, its ruling is that they accept it in all cases, whether it agrees with principles or not. A section: a rare transmission, its ruling is that they do not accept it unless it agrees with principles. A section: a derived opinion from the later scholars that the majority of the companions agreed upon, its ruling is that they give fatwa with it in all cases. A section: a derived opinion from them that the majority of the companions did not agree upon, its ruling is that the mufti should examine it against principles and parallels; if he finds it in agreement, he takes it, otherwise he leaves it. (Adab al-Ifta' for my father, Mazhir)
(3) His statement: 'Zahir al-Riwayah.' The meaning of Zahir al-Riwayah is the apparent transmission from the Imam that the trustworthy have transmitted, either by tawatur or by shuhra, as in Hashiyat al-Tahtawi on al-Durr al-Mukhtar.
Thus the idafa therein is inverted from description, like 'kabir al-hajm' which is in the meaning of 'hajm kabir'.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage presents the three-layer classification of Hanafi masail. The first layer is Masail al-Usul (Zahir al-Riwayah) — the most authoritative rulings transmitted directly from Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. The commentary adds that the term 'ashabuna' usually refers to these three imams. It also notes an alternative four-fold division from Adab al-Ifta', which distinguishes between established rulings, rare transmissions, agreed-upon later derivations, and disputed derivations. Finally, it gives a linguistic note on the term 'Zahir al-Riwayah', explaining it as a descriptive phrase (idafa maqluba). The overall purpose is to guide muftis on which rulings carry the most weight.

Key Terms
طبقات المسائل (Ṭabaqāt al-Masāʾil): Three hierarchical categories of Hanafi rulings: Masail al-Usul, Nawadir, and Nawazil (though only first is fully discussed here).
مسائل الأصول (Masāʾil al-Uṣūl): The foundational rulings transmitted from the three imams; synonymous with Zahir al-Riwayah.
أصحابنا (Aṣḥābnā): In this context, primarily the three imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani.
ظاهر الرواية (Zāhir al-Riwāyah): The apparent/well-known transmission from the imams, transmitted by tawatur or shuhra, forming the most authoritative layer of masail.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Nawazil
B) Nawadir
C) Masail al-Usul (Zahir al-Riwayah)
D) All three equally

Key Takeaway
Zahir al-Riwayah is the highest authority in Hanafi fatwa and must be followed without further verification; other layers require scrutiny against usul.

8 min
The Three Levels of Hanafi Legal Issues (Tabaqat al-Masa'il)
Classification of Hanafi legal issues by authority level

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and distinguish between Zahir al-Riwayah and al-Nawadir, and explain their authority in issuing fatwa.

Core Idea
Not all Hanafi rulings are equal; the mufti must prioritize based on transmission strength.

In the Hanafi tradition, legal issues are hierarchically classified by authority. This lesson introduces the first two levels: Masail al-Usul (Zahir al-Riwayah) and Masail al-Nawadir. Understanding this classification is essential for a mufti to know which ruling to prioritize when issuing a fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall classification
The text states that Hanafi masail are on three levels. Focus on the first two: Zahir al-Riwayah and al-Nawadir. Note that the third level is mentioned but not detailed here.
The third level will be covered in subsequent lessons.
2
Define the first level (Zahir al-Riwayah)
Identify its sources: the six books of Imam Muhammad (al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, etc.). Recognize its narrators: the three imams (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). Understand its authority: transmitted by tawatur or shuhra, so it is definitively acted upon.
Zufar and Hasan are sometimes included but the prevalent view is the three.
3
Define the second level (al-Nawadir)
Identify its sources: other books by Muhammad (e.g., al-Kaysaniyat, al-Haruniyat). Recognize that these are also from the founders but not in the six books. Their acceptance is conditional: they must agree with the principles (usul).
Later reliable compilations (Tahawi, Karkhi) are attached to the usul level.
4
Understand the role of later compilations
The text notes that abridgements by later reliable scholars (e.g., al-Tahawi, al-Karkhi, al-Quduri) are considered equivalent to Zahir al-Riwayah in reliability due to their careful transmission.
This is an important nuance for fatwa.
5
Apply the classification
As a mufti, when faced with a ruling: first check Zahir al-Riwayah (the six books). If not found there, check al-Nawadir, but only if it aligns with the principles. The third level (not covered) would be next.
This hierarchy prevents arbitrary selection of rulings.

فالإضافة فيه مقلوب من التوصيف ككبير الحجم فإنه في معنى حجم كبير

أن يكون قول الثلاثة، أو قول بعضهم ) . ثم هذه المسائل (۲) التي تسمى بظاهر الرواية والأصول، هى ما وجد في كتب محمد التي هي "المبسوط"، و "الزيادات " ، و "الجامع الصغير " ، و "السير الصغير"، و "الجامع الكبير " ، و "السير الكبير " . وإنما سميت بظاهر الرواية ؛ لأنها رويت عن محمد برواية الثقات، فهى ثابتة عنه إما متواترة أو مشهورة عنه .
الثانية: مسائل النوادر، وهي مسائل مروية عن أصحاب المذهب المذكورين، لكن لا في الكتب المذكورة ، بل إما في كتب أخر لمحمد (۳) غيرها كالكيسانيات، والهارونيات والجرجانيات، والرقيات (٤). وإنما قيل لها :
(۱) قوله : " أو قول بعضهم الأولى حذفه كما يدل عليه السباق، وإلا لا يصح معنى الاستدراك، ويؤيد ذلك ما في رد المحتار من قوله : "لكن الغالب الشائع في ظاهر
الرواية أن يكون قول الثلاثة " ، فلم يذكر ههنا لفظ " أو قول بعضهم " . Topic: The levels of legal issues are three. Know that the legal issues of our companions (1) the Hanafis are on three levels (2): First: Issues of the principles, also called Zahir al-Riwayah (3), and they are issues narrated from the founders of the school, who are Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on them, and they are called 'the three scholars'. Zufar, Hasan, and others who took fiqh from Abu Hanifa may be joined to them, but the prevalent in Zahir al-Riwayah is that it is the statement of the three or the statement of some of them. Then these issues (2) that are called Zahir al-Riwayah and principles are what is found in the books of Muhammad which are: al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Kabir. They are called Zahir al-Riwayah because they were narrated from Muhammad by reliable narrators, so they are established from him either by tawatur or by fame. Second: Issues of al-Nawadir, and they are issues narrated from the aforementioned founders of the school, but not in the mentioned books, rather in other books of Muhammad (3) other than them, such as al-Kaysaniyat, al-Haruniyat, al-Jurjaniyat, and al-Raqiyat (4). They are called thus...
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the classification of Hanafi legal issues into three levels, a core concept in the methodology of ifta. The author states that the issues of the Hanafi school are on three levels. The first level is Masail al-Usul, also known as Zahir al-Riwayah. These are the issues narrated from the three main founders: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Occasionally, other early students like Zufar and Hasan are included, but the prevalent in Zahir al-Riwayah is that it comprises the statements of the three or some of them. The text clarifies that these issues are found in the six books of Imam Muhammad: al-Mabsut, al-Ziyadat, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Jami' al-Kabir, and al-Siyar al-Kabir. They are called Zahir al-Riwayah because they were transmitted from Muhammad through reliable chains, either by tawatur (mass transmission) or by shuhra (widespread fame). The second level is Masail al-Nawadir, which are issues also narrated from the founders but not found in the six books. Instead, they are found in other books by Muhammad such as al-Kaysaniyat, al-Haruniyat, al-Jurjaniyat, and al-Raqiyat. The passage continues to describe that the abridgements made by later reliable scholars (like al-Tahawi, al-Karkhi, etc.) are attached to the level of usul due to their reliability. The third level is mentioned but the passage cuts off before its definition. The footnotes provide additional clarifications: the term 'our companions' normally refers to the three imams; there is an alternative division into four categories; and the meaning of Zahir al-Riwayah is explained. Overall, this is a fundamental classification for a mufti to determine the weight of different rulings.

Key Terms
طبقات المسائل (Tabaqat al-Masa'il): The levels of legal issues in the Hanafi school, categorized by their authority and transmission
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The well-known narrations from the three imams found in the six books of Muhammad al-Shaybani
النوادر (al-Nawadir): Rare narrations from the imams not in the six books but in other works by Muhammad or later scholars

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is a characteristic of Zahir al-Riwayah?
A) They are found in books like al-Kaysaniyat.
B) They are narrated only from Abu Hanifa.
C) They are found in the six books of Imam Muhammad.
D) They are of lower authority than al-Nawadir.

Key Takeaway
A mufti must prioritize Zahir al-Riwayah (the six books) and only use al-Nawadir if it aligns with the principles.
